Interpreting the Particle Ba for Attachment in Conditional Divorce
Analyses the particle ba as conditional rather than causative in divorce formulas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that the primary meaning of the particle 'ba' is attachment (ilṣāq) to explain why conditional divorces with divine phrases do not take effect immediately.

Core Idea
The particle 'ba' primarily indicates attachment, not causation; uncertainty in the condition suspends the divorce.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the interpretation of common Arabic particles can shape entire rulings. This lesson explores a key dispute over the particle 'ba' in conditional divorce phrases like 'bi-mashī'ati Llāh'. Does it make the divorce occur immediately (causation) or suspend it upon an unknown condition (attachment)? The Hanafi school argues that the primary meaning of 'ba' is attachment, implying temporal sequence, which supports a conditional reading and prevents the divorce from taking effect. This analysis draws on Quranic usage and logical priority.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
When a husband says 'you are divorced by the will of Allah' or 'by His decree', the Hanafi ruling is that the divorce does not occur. The particle 'ba' is interpreted as indicating attachment (ilṣāq) to a condition, not causation.
This ruling is found in the original matn being commented on.
2
Identify the opposing argument
An opponent argues that 'ba' can mean causation (sababiyyah), as in Quran 5:38 'jazā'an bimā kasabā', and thus the divorce should take effect immediately.
The opponent's dalil is the Quranic usage of 'ba' for cause.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: primary meaning and temporal sequence
The Hanafi response argues that the primary meaning of 'ba' is attachment, which implies a temporal sequence: the attached thing precedes what it is attached to. In a condition, the condition (Allah's will) must precede the conditioned (divorce), so sequence exists. In causation, cause and effect are simultaneous, which is not the case here. Therefore the conditional interpretation is preferable.
The reasoning uses qiyās jaliy (manifest analogy) based on the core meaning of the particle.
4
Apply the concept of uncertainty
Even if the condition is valid, its existence (Allah's will) is unknown and uncertain. Just as an unclear condition suspends a suspended matter, here the divorce does not occur because the condition is not known to be fulfilled.
This parallels the principle that a suspended act does not occur without knowledge of the condition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to the Hanafi position, such conditional divorces do not take effect. According to the opposing (hypothetical) view, they might take effect immediately.
This shows how a seemingly minor linguistic point leads to a significant difference in fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو «بإرادة الله تعالى» أو «بحكمه» لم تطلق. أي الجلالة. لعدم إدراك وجود الشرط. فصل حرف الباء للإلصاق (١) قوله: [لم تطلق] فإن قلت: هلا حملت الباء في مسئلة المشية وأخواتها على السببية؛ لأنها قد تستعمل بمعنى السببية قال تعالى: جَزَاءً بِمَا كَسَبَا [المائدة: ٣٨] وإذا حملت على ما قلنا تطلق في الحال، قلنا: الحمل على الشرط أولى؛ لأنه أقرب إلى الإلصاق وجه الأولوية أن في الإلصاق معنى الترتيب؛ لأنه يقتضي ملصقاً مقدماً به على الملصق زماناً ليتمكن الإلصاق وبه الترتيب الزماني في الشرط والمشروط موجود بخلاف العلة مع المعلول؛ لأن العلة مقارنة مع المعلول زماناً، كذا قيل. (٢) قوله: [لم تطلق] لأن الإلصاق بمشية الله تعالى قيد بوقوع الطلاق والمقيد لا يوجد ولا يتم وجوده بدون القيد خارجاً كان أو داخلاً ووجود القيد متردد فيه غير معلوم فلا يقع بدون العلم كما في جهالة الشرط في المعلق عليه، فهذه الباء أفادت معنى التعليق إفادةً بالعرض، كذا في "الفصول".
Or 'by the will of Allah' or 'by His decree' does not occur as divorce. That is, the Majesty. Due to non-realization of the condition. Section: The letter ba for attachment. (1) His statement: [did not divorce] If you say: Why not interpret the ba in the issue of the will and its sisters as causative? Because it is sometimes used in the sense of causation, Allah said: 'as a recompense for what they earned' [5:38]. And if interpreted as we said, it would occur immediately. We say: Interpreting it as conditional is better because it is closer to attachment. The priority is that in attachment there is the meaning of sequence; because it requires an attached thing preceded in time by what it is attached to for attachment to be possible; and temporal sequence exists in the condition and the conditioned, unlike cause and effect because cause is simultaneous with effect in time. So it is said. (2) His statement: [did not divorce] Because attachment to the will of Allah is a condition for the occurrence of divorce, and the conditioned cannot exist nor be fully realized without the condition, whether external or internal, and the existence of the condition is uncertain and unknown, so it does not occur without knowledge, just as in the case of ignorance of the condition in the suspended upon. So this ba imparted the meaning of conditional suspension indirectly, as in 'al-Fusul'.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the particle 'ba' in conditional divorce formulas. The original matn states that if a husband says 'you are divorced by the will of Allah' or 'by His decree', the divorce does not take place. The commentator explains the reasoning. He addresses an objection: why not interpret 'ba' as causative (sababiyyah) so that divorce occurs immediately? The answer: interpreting it as conditional (shart) is preferable because the primary meaning of 'ba' is attachment (ilṣāq), and attachment implies temporal sequence (taratub). In a condition, the condition precedes the conditioned in time, whereas cause and effect are simultaneous. Since the existence of the condition (Allah's will) is unknown, the divorce does not occur. This is similar to a known principle: if a condition is unknown, the suspended matter does not occur. Thus, 'ba' here indirectly indicates suspension (ta'liq). The analysis relies on Quran 5:38 as an example of 'ba' for causation, but favors the conditional interpretation through logical priority (qiyās jaliy) and istihsan?.

Key Terms
الباء (al-bā'): The letter 'ba' used as a preposition; its primary meaning is attachment (ilṣāq).
الإلصاق (al-ilṣāq): Linguistic attachment; the literal meaning of the particle 'ba'.
السببية (as-sababiyyah): Causation; the use of 'ba' to indicate cause (e.g., 'recompense for what they earned').

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of the particle 'ba' as indicating attachment rather than causation is key to understanding why conditional divorces with divine phrases do not take effect due to uncertainty of the condition.

Types of Bayan: Understanding Bayan Taqrir
Definition and classification of bayan into seven types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish bayan taqrir from other types of bayan and apply it to examples from Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Bayan taqrir confirms the apparent meaning without changing the ruling.

In Hanafi usul, al-bayan is the clarification of intended meaning. The Lawgiver communicates through texts that sometimes carry multiple possibilities. This lesson introduces the seven types of bayan, with special attention to bayan taqrir—the type that reinforces the apparent meaning to exclude all other interpretations. Through examples from financial transactions, you'll see how tahqiq al-manat operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Situate bayan in usul al-fiqh
Bayan is needed when a text has an apparent meaning but admits other possibilities. It is the act of clarifying the intended meaning by a qualified authority.
2
Memorize the seven categories
The text lists them: taqrir, tafsir, taghyir, darura, hal, atf, tabdil. This classification is unique to Hanafi usul.
Keep this list handy for future reference.
3
Parse the definition of bayan taqrir
It occurs when the apparent meaning is reinforced to cut off any remote possibility. Note: it does not introduce a new ruling.
The key phrase: 'yabiynu al-murad bima yaqta' al-ihtimal'.
4
Examine the first example: qafiz and currency
A debt of a qafiz of wheat is absolute; stating 'qafiz al-balad' confirms it's the local standard. This closes the door to other interpretations.
The word 'qafiz' alone could refer to any measure; the clarification pins it to the local one.
5
Examine the second example: wadi'a vs. amana
The word 'indi' alone could imply trust; specifying 'wadi'a' clarifies the legal relationship. Both examples show that the ruling remains unchanged.
Bayan taqrir does not alter the hukm; it only confirms the apparent meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في وجوه البيان، البيان على سبعة أنواع: بيان تقرير وبيان تفسير وبيان تغيير وبيان ضرورة وبيان حال وبيان عطف وبيان تبديل". قال الشارح: وأمّا الأوّل فهو أن يكون معنى اللفظ ظاهرا لكنّه يحتمل غيره فبيّن المراد بما يقطع الاحتمال. ومثال ذلك إذا قال: «لفلان على قفيز حنطة بقفيز البلد» أو «ألف من نقد البلد» فإنه يكون بيان تقرير؛ لأن المطلق محمول على قفيز البلد ونقده مع احتمال إرادة الغير، فإذا بين ذلك انسد باب التأويل والاحتمال. وكذلك لو قال: لفلان عندي ألف وديعة فإن كلمة «عندي» كانت بإطلاقها تفيد الأمانة مع احتمال إرادة الغير فإذا قال: «وديعة» فقد قرّر حكم الظاهر ببيانه.
Chapter on the types of bayan (clarification). Bayan is of seven types: 1) Bayan Taqrir (confirming clarification), 2) Bayan Tafsir (explanatory clarification), 3) Bayan Taghyir (altering clarification), 4) Bayan Darura (necessity clarification), 5) Bayan Hal (circumstantial clarification), 6) Bayan Atf (conjunctive clarification), 7) Bayan Tabdil (substitutive clarification). The commentator said: As for the first (type), it is when the meaning of the word is apparent but still admits another possibility, so the intended meaning is clarified by what cuts off that possibility. Its example: if someone says, "So-and-so has on me a qafiz of wheat according to the qafiz of the country" or "a thousand dirhams according to the currency of the country," then this is bayan taqrir because the absolute (expression) is carried upon the qafiz of the country and its currency while still admitting the possibility of intending another, so when he clarifies that, the door to interpretation and possibility is closed. Similarly, if he says, "So-and-so has with me (indi) a thousand as a deposit (wadi'a)," the word 'indi' by its absolute usage implies trust (amanah) while admitting the possibility of intending something else, so when he says 'wadi'a,' he has confirmed the ruling of the apparent meaning by his clarification.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi defines 'bayan' (clarification) and classifies it into seven types according to the Hanafi usul tradition. The author states that bayan is of seven types, then the commentator (احسن الحواشی) elaborates on the first type, bayan taqrir. Bayan taqrir applies when a word has an apparent meaning but still carries a remote possibility of another interpretation (such as metaphor or specification). The speaker then clarifies that the apparent meaning is indeed intended, thereby cutting off the possibility. Two examples are given: (1) An absolute debt (e.g., a qafiz of wheat) is normally understood according to the local standard, but there is a possibility another standard was meant; stating 'according to the qafiz of the country' removes that possibility. (2) The word 'indi' (with me) in the context of a debt implies trust/amanah, but could be misunderstood; adding 'wadi'a' (deposit) confirms the intended meaning. This type of bayan does not change the original ruling but reinforces it.

Key Terms
البيان (al-bayān): Clarification or explanation of the intended meaning of a word or text.
بيان تقرير (bayān taqrīr): Confirming clarification: when an apparent meaning is reinforced to exclude any other possibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Bayan Tafsir
B) Bayan Taqrir
C) Bayan Taghyir
D) Bayan Tabdil

Key Takeaway
Bayan taqrir is a confirming clarification that does not create new law but reaffirms the apparent meaning against remote possibilities.

Bayan al-Taqrir: Definition and Examples
Defines bayan al-taqrir with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define bayan al-taqrir and identify it in legal statements, distinguishing it from other types of bayan.

Core Idea
Bayan al-taqrir confirms the apparent meaning of a word, shutting the door to alternative interpretations.

In Hanafi usul, explanations (bayan) are categorized by the kind of clarity they bring. Bayan al-taqrir is used when a word is already apparent (zahir) but could be misunderstood. This lesson explains how it works using examples from contracts and deposits.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the context
Identify a statement that contains a word that is clear in its customary meaning but could possibly refer to something else.
The word must be mutlaq or zahir, not completely ambiguous.
2
Identify the bayan
Find the explicit clarification that confirms the apparent meaning, leaving no doubt about the speaker's intent.
The bayan restates the word with specification (e.g., 'qafiz of the town' instead of just 'qafiz').
3
Confirm the effect
Verify that after the bayan, the possibility of alternative interpretation is eliminated.
This makes the ruling based on the apparent meaning definitive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في وجوه البيان
هو الظاهر فيتقرّر حكم الظاهر ببيانه ومثاله إذا قال: «لفلان على قفيز حنطة بقفيز البلد» أو «ألف من نقد البلد فإنه يكون بيان تقرير؛ لأن المطلق بتبادره. وإن كان محمولا على قفيز البلد ونقده مع احتمال إرادة الغير، فإذا بين ذلك انسد باب التأويل والاحتمال. فقد قرره ببيانه وكذلك لو قال: لفلان عندي ألف وديعة فإن كلمة «عندي» كانت بإطلاقها تفيد الأمانة مع احتمال إرادة الغير فإذا قال: «وديعة» فقد قرّر حكم الظاهر ببيانه.
(۱) قوله: [فقد قرّره ببيانه] لأنّ مطلق القفيز ومطلق الألف كان محمولاً على قفيز البلد ونقد البلـــد؛ لأنّ ذلك المطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف والمتعارف قفيز البلد ونقد البلد، فهذا حقيقة اللفظ العرفية لكن مع يحتمل إرادة الغير بأن يراد قفيز بلد آخر ونقده، فإذا بين ذلك قفيز البلد ونقد البلد كان بيان تقرير الكلام على ظاهر مراده وكذا المثال الآتي؛ لأنّ كلمة «عندي» للحضرة تفيد الحفظ والأمانة، وبقوله: «وديعة» قرّر ذلك، كذا في "الفصول".
Chapter on the Types of Bayan (Explanation). It is the apparent (zahir) so the ruling of the apparent is confirmed by its bayan. Example: if someone says, 'For so-and-so is a qafiz of wheat according to the qafiz of the town' or 'one thousand according to the currency of the town,' then this is bayan al-taqrir because the absolute (mutlaq) is understood by its immediate association. And if it is carried on the qafiz of the town and its currency while there is a possibility of intending something else, then when he explains that, the door of interpretation and possibility is closed. He has confirmed it by his bayan. Similarly, if someone says, 'I have one thousand as a deposit with me,' the word 'with me' in its absoluteness indicates trusteeship (amanah) with the possibility of intending something else. So when he says 'deposit,' he has confirmed the ruling of the apparent by his bayan. (Footnote: His saying 'he confirmed it by his bayan' because the absolute qafiz and absolute thousand are carried on the qafiz of the town and the currency of the town because the absolute turns to the customary, and the customary is the qafiz of the town and the currency of the town. This is the real meaning of the customary word, but with the possibility of intending something else, like intending the qafiz of another town and its currency. So when he explains that it is the qafiz of the town and its currency, it becomes a bayan al-taqrir of the speech according to the apparent meaning he intended. Likewise the following example, because the word 'with me' indicates presence, which implies preservation and trusteeship, and by his saying 'deposit' he confirms that. As in 'al-Fusul'.)
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage defines bayan al-taqrir, one of the types of bayan (explanation) in Hanafi usul. It occurs when a word is already clear (zahir) but has a slight possibility of another interpretation. The speaker then explicitly mentions the intended meaning, thereby confirming the apparent ruling and closing the door to alternative interpretations. The example given is a debt contract: if someone says 'a qafiz of wheat' without specification, the default is the local qafiz, but it could possibly mean another. Stating 'according to the qafiz of the town' makes it definite. Similarly, saying 'I have a thousand with me' implies a deposit (amanah), but affirming 'as a deposit' confirms it. The footnote clarifies that the absolute (mutlaq) is understood customarily, and the bayan removes any ambiguity.

Key Terms
بيان التقرير (bayan al-taqrir): An explanation that confirms the apparent meaning of a word, removing the possibility of alternative interpretation.
ظاهر (zahir): A word that is clear in its meaning but still open to possible alternative interpretation.
مطلق (mutlaq): An absolute term that is unrestricted and carries a customary meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Bayan al-taqrir confirms the apparent meaning of a word that is already clear but could be misinterpreted, making the legal ruling definitive.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Ta'liq (Suspension) in Bayan al-Taghyir
Defines bayan al-taghyir and disputes the nature of ta'liq between Hanafis and Shafi'is.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the nature of a suspended (mu'allaq) utterance, explain each school's reasoning, and apply the Hanafi rule to the case of a suspension involving a non-related woman or another's slave.

Core Idea
A suspended utterance is not a cause in the present; it becomes a cause only when the condition occurs.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi introduces the concept of bayan al-taghyir, where a clarifying statement changes the meaning of the original. The key example is ta'liq (suspension), where a condition delays the effect of a divorce or emancipation pronouncement. The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ fundamentally: do the words create a cause in the present that is merely blocked by the condition, or do they create no cause until the condition is fulfilled? Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping how Hanafi usul treats conditional legal speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two schools' positions
State what the Hanafis and Shafi'is each claim about the time when the suspended utterance becomes a cause.
2
Analyze the proofs
For each school, identify the key analogy or argument they use to support their view (e.g., the impossibility of effect lagging behind cause for Hanafis; the immediate effect if condition were removed for Shafi'is).
3
Apply to the practical example
Consider the case of saying to a non-related woman "If I marry you, you are divorced." Predict the outcome under each school's theory.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi condition
Understand why the Hanafis require the suspension to be connected to ownership or a cause of ownership when the locus is absent at the time of utterance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما بيان التغيير فهو أن يتغيّر ببيانه معنى كلامه ونظيره التعليق والاستثناء، وقد اختلف الفقهاء في الفصلين فقال أصحابنا: المعلق بالشرط سبب عند وجود الشرط لا قبله وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : التعليق موجب لوقوع الطلاق سبب في الحال إلا أن عدم الشرط مانع من حكمه، وفائدة الخلاف تظهر بيننا وبين الشافعي رحمه الله.
(۱) قوله: [التعليق] أي: بشرط مثل قوله : «أنت حرّ إن دخلت الدار» فإن قوله : «أنت حرّ» مقتضاه نزول العتق؛ لأنّ الإيجاب علّة لثبوت موجبه والمعلول لا يتخلّف عن علّة ولو بزمان قليل، فإذا ذكر الشرط بعد ذلك وهو قوله: «إن دخلت الدار لا يعتق في الحال وتأخر موجبه إلى زمان وجود الشرط فكان تغييراً لموجبه بطريق البيان، كذا في "المعدن".
(۲) قوله: [ والاستثناء] مثل قوله : «لفلان علي ألف إلا مئة فإنّ قوله : «لفلان علي ألف» موجبه وجوب الألف بتمامه وبقوله: «إلأمئة» تغيّر معناه من التمام إلى البعض، كذا في "المعدن".
(۳) قوله عند وجود الشرط... إلخ وهو دخول الدار لا قبله فكان قوله : أنت طالق» غير موجود قبل وجود الشرط، وإنما يصير سبباً عند وجود الشرط فكان عدم الحكم وهو وقوع الطلاق بناء على العدم الأصلي الذي كان قبل التعليق لا بناءً على عدَم الشرط؛ وهذا لأنّ الإيجاب إنما ينعقــــد باعتبار صدوره من أهله في محلّه، فإذا لم يصل إلى محله لا سبباً كما إذا أضيف إلى غير محله بأن يصير كان بهميةً أو ميتةً، كذا في "المعدن".
(٤) قوله: [وقال الشافعي ... إلخ وهو يقول : إن المعلق بالشرط أي: الإيجاب وهو قوله: «أنت طالق» سبب في الحال أي: سبب موجب لوقوع الطلاق؛ لأنه لولا الشرط لوقع الطلاق في الحال لا محالة، لكنّ التعليق منع وجود الحكم وآخره إلى زمان وجود الشرط فكان عدم الحكم مضافاً إلى عدم الشرط لأن يكون عدماً للعدم الأصلي، ونحن نقول: المعلق بالشرط لا ينعقد سبباً موجباً للحكم في الحال؛ لأنّ التعليق يمنع عن انعقاد الإيجاب سبباً، فكان قوله: «أنت طالق» غير موجود قبل وجود الشرط، وإنمــــا وجود الشرط فكان عدم الحكم كوقوع الطلاق والحرّية بناء على العدم الأصلي الذي كان قبل التعليق لا بناء على عدم الشرط، كذا في كتب الأصول.
(٥) قوله: [مانع من حكمه... آه] أي من وقوع الطلاق إلى زمان وجود الشرط؛ وذلك لأن قوله: «أنت طالق كلام وضع لرفع قيد النكاح شرعاً، وهذا الكلام يوجد حسنًا مع الشرط فلا معنى لإخراجه عن موضعه.
فصل وأما بيان التغيير فيما إذا قال لأجنبية: «إن تزوّجتك فأنت طالق أو قال لعبد الغير: «إن ملكتك فأنت حر ، يكون التعليق باطلا عنده؛ لأن حكم التعليق انعقاد صدر الكلام علة والطلاق والعتاق ههنا لم ينعقد علة لعدم إضافته إلى المحل المذكور. فبطل حكم التعليق فلا يصح التعليق، وعندنا كان التعليق صحيحا حتى إذا تزوجها يقع الطلاق؛ لأن كلامه إنما ينعقد علة عند وجود الشرط والملك لوجود الشرط وهو التزوج ثابت عند وجود الشرط فيصحّ التعليق، ولهذا المعنى قلنا: شرط صحة التعليق للوقوع في صورة عدم الملك أن يكون مضافا إلى الملك أو إلى سبب الملك.
Chapter: As for the explanation of al-taghyir (change), it is that the meaning of one's speech is changed by its clarification, and its examples are ta'liq (suspension) and istithna (exception). The jurists disagreed on these two categories. Our companions (the Hanafis) said: The suspended (mua'allaq) by a condition is a cause at the existence of the condition, not before it. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The suspension necessitates the occurrence of divorce; it is a cause in the present, except that the non-existence of the condition is a preventer of its effect. The benefit of the disagreement appears between us and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him.
(1) His statement: [al-ta'liq] i.e., by a condition, like his saying: 'You are free if you enter the house.' For his saying 'You are free' necessitates the descent of emancipation, because the utterance (ijab) is a cause for the establishment of its effect, and the effect does not lag behind its cause even for a short time. So when he mentions the condition after that, which is his saying 'if you enter the house,' he is not freed immediately, and its effect is delayed until the time of the condition's existence. Thus it becomes a change (taghyir) of its effect by way of clarification (bayan). From al-Ma'din.
(2) His statement: [and al-istithna'] like his saying: 'So-and-so owes me one thousand except one hundred.' For his saying 'So-and-so owes me one thousand' necessitates the obligation of the full thousand, and by his saying 'except one hundred' its meaning changes from completeness to partial. From al-Ma'din.
(3) His statement: 'at the existence of the condition... etc.' i.e., when he enters the house, not before. So his statement 'you are divorced' is non-existent before the condition's existence, and it only becomes a cause at the condition's existence. Thus the non-existence of the ruling, which is the occurrence of divorce, is based on the original non-existence that was there before the suspension, not based on the non-existence of the condition. This is because the utterance (ijab) is only constituted by being issued from its proper person and applied to its proper locus (mahall). So if it does not reach its locus, it is not a cause, just as if it were added to something not its locus, such as a beast or a carcass. From al-Ma'din.
(4) His statement: [al-Shafi'i said... etc.] He says that the suspended by a condition, i.e., the utterance (ijab) which is his saying 'you are divorced,' is a cause in the present, i.e., a cause necessitating the occurrence of divorce. Because were it not for the condition, divorce would occur immediately without doubt. However, the suspension prevents the existence of the ruling and delays it to the time of the condition's existence. So the non-existence of the ruling is attributed to the non-existence of the condition, not to the original non-existence. And we (Hanafis) say: The suspended by a condition does not become a cause necessitating the ruling in the present, because suspension prevents the utterance from being constituted as a cause. So his saying 'you are divorced' is non-existent before the condition's existence, and only becomes a cause at the condition's existence. Thus the non-existence of the ruling, like the occurrence of divorce and freedom, is based on the original non-existence that existed before the suspension, not based on the non-existence of the condition. From usul books.
(5) His statement: ['preventer of its effect'...] i.e., preventer of the occurrence of divorce until the time of the condition's existence. This is because his saying 'you are divorced' is speech placed to remove the bond of marriage legally, and this speech is appropriate when there is a condition. So there is no meaning in removing it from its context.
Chapter: As for the explanation of al-taghyir regarding when he says to a non-related woman: 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' or he says to another's slave: 'If I own you, you are free.' The suspension is invalid in his (al-Shafi'i's) view, because the effect of suspension is that the beginning of the speech becomes a cause, but divorce and emancipation here have not become a cause due to the lack of connection to the mentioned locus. So the ruling of suspension is nullified, and thus the suspension is not valid. In our view, the suspension is valid, such that when he marries her, divorce occurs. Because his speech only becomes a cause at the existence of the condition, and ownership exists at the condition's existence when he marries. So the suspension is valid. For this reason we said: The condition for the validity of suspension in the case of non-ownership is that it be connected to ownership or to a cause of ownership.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi, with the commentary of Ahsan al-Hawashi, addresses the concept of bayan al-taghyir—clarification that changes the meaning of a statement. The author presents two examples: ta'liq (suspension) and istithna (exception). The core of the discussion is the juristic disagreement on the nature of ta'liq. According to the Hanafi school, when a conditional statement like 'You are free if you enter the house' is made, the suspending clause prevents the utterance from being an effective cause until the condition occurs. The emancipation or divorce does not take effect in the present; instead, it becomes a cause only at the moment the condition is fulfilled. The non-occurrence of the effect before the condition is due to the original non-existence, not because the condition is a preventer. Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, argues that the suspended utterance is a cause in the present, but the condition acts as a preventer (mani') that delays the effect. The practical difference (fā'ida al-khilāf) between the two views appears in cases where the condition may never occur, or in matters like inheritance and other subsidiary rulings.

The passage then applies this principle to a specific scenario: someone says to a non-related woman, 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' or to another's slave, 'If I own you, you are free.' Al-Shafi'i considers such suspensions invalid because at the time of utterance, the woman is not a wife and the slave is not owned by the speaker—the cause (divorce or emancipation) is directed to a non-locus. In his view, the beginning of the speech must be a cause, and since the locus is missing, the cause cannot be constituted. The Hanafis, however, rule the suspension valid because the utterance does not need to be a cause at the moment of utterance; it only becomes a cause when the condition is met. At that time, the locus (marriage or ownership) exists. Hence, the suspension is sound. This also leads to the Hanafi condition that, in cases where the locus is not present at the time of utterance, the suspension must be attached to ownership or a cause of ownership (such as marriage contract or gift) so that the locus is available when the condition occurs.

The commentary (hawāshī) included in the text provides detailed reasoning: analogies from other invalid causes (like adding a sale to a corpse) and the principle that a cause must have a proper subject. The Hanafi position is based on the idea that the conditional utterance is not a cause in the present; it only becomes a cause upon the condition. Therefore, the lack of a present locus does not invalidate the suspension. Instead, it suffices that the locus will exist at the time the cause becomes effective.

Key Terms
بيان التغيير (bayan al-taghyir): A type of clarification (bayan) that changes the meaning of a previous statement, such that the effect is different from what the original wording would imply without the clarifier.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspending the effect of an utterance (like divorce or emancipation) on the occurrence of a future condition, e.g., 'You are divorced if you enter the house.'
الاستثناء (al-istithna): Exception, e.g., 'I owe you one thousand except one hundred,' which partially excludes a part from the previous statement.
السبب (al-sabab): A cause that necessitates the ruling when its conditions are met and preventers are absent. Here, the utterance of 'You are free' is a cause for emancipation.
المانع (al-mani'): A preventer that blocks the effect of a cause despite the cause being present. According to al-Shafi'i, the non-existence of the condition is a preventer.
الحكم (al-hukm): The ruling, i.e., the occurrence of divorce or emancipation, which is the effect of the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a man says to a non-related woman, 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' and then later marries her, what happens?
A) The divorce does not occur because the suspension was invalid from the start.
B) The divorce occurs at the time of the utterance because the cause was present.
C) The divorce occurs upon marriage because the cause becomes effective at the condition's occurrence.
D) The divorce is suspended and never occurs because the woman was a non-related woman.

Key Takeaway
A suspended utterance in Hanafi usul does not create a cause until its condition is met and its proper locus exists; this is the essence of bayan al-taghyir.

Wasf as Ta‘līq: The Hanafi-Shāfi‘ī Dispute on Marrying a Kitābī Slave Woman
Explains that a description functions like a condition and applies it to the ruling on marrying a Kitābī slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a description (wasf) does not imply negation when absent (rejecting mafhūm al-mukhālafa) and evaluate the Shāfi‘ī counter-argument using the case of marrying a Kitābī slave woman.

Core Idea
A description in a text affirms the ruling when present; it does not negate when absent — Hanafis rely on general proofs.

This passage addresses a core usul dispute: does a qualified text (nass muqayyad) automatically negate the ruling when the qualification is absent? The Hanafis say no; the Shāfi‘īs say yes. The practical thamarah is the permissibility of marrying a Kitābī slave woman. The source presents the principles and the proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on wasf
A description (wasf) like 'believing' in 4:25 functions to establish the ruling when present but does not negate when absent. The ruling for other cases is derived from general proofs.
The Hanafi position is that wasf is like a condition in establishing the ruling, but not in negating it.
2
Identify the Shāfi‘ī position
The Shāfi‘īs hold that the description acts as a condition; its absence negates the ruling. They rely on the qualified text as exclusive.
This is based on the principle that a condition (shart) necessitates the absence of the conditioned when absent.
3
Examine the proofs
Hanafi proof: general texts (4:24, 4:3) allow marriage to women; the qualified text (4:25) is interpreted as recommendation (istihbāb). Shāfi‘ī proof: the qualified text restricts the ruling to believing slave women, implying prohibition of others.
Pay attention to how each school prioritizes the texts.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the general texts are not abrogated by the qualified text; the qualified text does not negate because the ruling can be derived from other causes. The restriction is for recommendation, not a condition.
The key is the Hanafi rejection of mafhūm al-mukhālafa as a binding proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis permit marriage to a Kitābī slave woman; Shāfi‘īs prohibit it.
This shows how a usul difference produces a concrete fiqh difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما بيان التغيير (1) الحكم بدليله فيجوز نكاح الأمة ويجب الإنفاق بالعمومات (2) ومن توابع هذا النوع أي من توابع التعليق بالشرط ترتب الحكم على اسم موصوف، وإنما كان من توابعه؛ لأنّ الوصف بمعنى الشرط متعلّق الحكم به كما بالشرط، بيانه أنه إذا قال: «أنت طالق راكبةً» فإنه بمنزلة قوله : أنت طالق إن ركبت» فإذا كان بمعنى الشرط كان الاختلاف في التعليق في الوصف. (3) قوله : [بصفة ... إلخ المراد بالموصوف والصفة المعنويان لا النحويان فيعم الحال وذا الحال والغاية والمغيا والموصول والصلة والفعل وفاعله ومفعوله ومتعلقاته والاسم التام والتمييز وغيرها. (4) قوله: [فإنه... إلخ] وإنما كان من توابعه؛ لأنّ الوصف بمعنى الشرط لتعليق الحكم به كما بالشرط فإنه لولا الوصف لثبت الحكم بمطلق الاسم كما أنه لولا الشرط لثبت الحكم في الحال، فلما ظهر للوصف أثر المنع كما ظهر للشرط ألحق به فعدم الوصف يوجب عدم الحكم كما أن عدم الشرط يوجب عدم الحكم و بيان كون الوصف بمعنى الشرط أنه إذا قال: «أنت طالق راكبة بمنزلة قوله: «أنت طالق إن ركبت» فإذا كان بمعنى الشرط كان الاختلاف في التعليق اختلافا في الوصف.  فصل وأما بيان التغيير أي الشافعي رحمه الله. الحكم بذلك الوصف عنده، وعلى هذا قال الشافعي رحمه الله: لا يجوز نكاح الأمة الكتابية؛ لأن النص رتب الحكم على أمة مؤمنة لقوله تعالى: ﴿مِن فَتَيَاتِكُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَات﴾ [النساء: ٢٥] فيتقيد بالمؤمنة فيمتنع الحكم عند عدم الوصف فلا يجوز نكاح الأمة الكتابية. (2) قوله: [فيمتنع الحكم عند عدم الوصف... آه] وعند عدم الوصف لا يوجب عدم الحكم كما أن عدم الشرط لا يوجب عدم المشروط، فقلنا: ثبت بهذا النص جواز نكاح الأمة المؤمنة، أما نكاح الفتاة الكافرة فلا يتعرّض النص له بالنفي والإثبات فيثبت جواز نكاحها بالعمومات وهي قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُحِلَّ لَكُم مَّا وَرَاء ذَلِكُمْ﴾ [النساء: ٢٤] وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَانكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُم مِّنَ النِّسَاء﴾ [النساء: ٣] والتقييد بالإيمان في النص للاستحباب بدليل أن الإيمان ليس بشرط في الحرائر بالاتفاق مع التقييد بقوله: ﴿الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾.
Chapter: Explanation of Change (1) The ruling by its proof: so it is permissible to marry a slave woman and obligatory to provide maintenance by general texts. (2) Among the corollaries of this type, i.e., among the corollaries of suspension by a condition, is the attachment of a ruling to a noun described by an attribute. This is a corollary because the attribute is like a condition upon which the ruling depends, just like the condition. Its clarification: if he says, 'You are divorced while riding,' it is like saying 'You are divorced if you ride.' So if it is like a condition, then disagreement on suspension is disagreement on the attribute. (3) The intended meaning of 'described' and 'attribute' is the semantic ones, not the syntactic; thus it includes the state and the subject of the state, the limit and the limited, the relative pronoun and its clause, the verb with its subject and object and their attachments, the complete noun, the specification, etc. (4) It is a corollary because the attribute is like a condition in suspending the ruling, since without the attribute the ruling would be established by the absolute noun, just as without the condition the ruling would be established immediately. When the attribute shows a preventing effect, it is attached to the condition. So the absence of the attribute entails the absence of the ruling, just as the absence of the condition entails the absence of the ruling. The clarification that the attribute is like a condition: if he says 'You are divorced while riding,' it is like 'You are divorced if you ride.' So if it is like a condition, disagreement on suspension is disagreement on the attribute. [Page 197] Chapter: Explanation of Change, i.e., al-Shafi‘i. The ruling by that attribute according to him. Based on this, al-Shafi‘i said: It is not permissible to marry a Kitābī slave woman because the text attaches the ruling to a believing slave woman, as in His statement: 'from your believing slave girls' [4:25]. So it is restricted to the believing one, so the ruling is prevented when the attribute is absent, and so it is not permissible to marry a Kitābī slave woman. (2) The absence of the attribute does not necessitate the absence of the ruling, just as the absence of the condition does not necessitate the absence of the conditioned. So we say: By this text the permissibility of marrying a believing slave woman is established. As for marrying an unbelieving slave woman, the text does not address it either by negation or affirmation, so its permissibility is established by the general texts, which are His statement: 'Lawful to you are all beyond these' [4:24] and His statement: 'Marry such women as seem good to you' [4:3]. The restriction to belief in the text is for recommendation, as evidence that belief is not a condition for free women by consensus despite the restriction in His statement: 'the chaste believing women'.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a madhhab dispute (usul al-fiqh) between the Hanafis and al-Shafi‘i over the interpretation of a qualified text. The Hanafis hold that a description (wasf) used in a ruling functions like a condition (shart), but they do not adopt mafhūm al-mukhālafa. Therefore, when the Quran mentions 'believing slave girls' (al-mu’mināt) in the context of marrying slave women, this does not negate the permissibility of marrying a Kitābī (Jewish or Christian) slave woman. According to the Hanafis, the ruling for the Kitābī slave woman is derived from the general proofs (al-‘umūmāt) that allow marriage to women and slave women. Al-Shafi‘i, by contrast, takes the qualified text as establishing that the condition (belief) must be present, and its absence negates the ruling. The passage explains the principle that a description is like a condition, but the Hanafis emphasize that this only establishes the ruling when the description is present; it does not prove the opposite (mafhūm al-mukhālafa). The commentary provides the Hanafi proof: the restriction to belief in the verse is for recommendation (istihbāb), not a condition, as shown by the fact that belief is not a condition for free women despite the similar restriction in another verse.

Key Terms
الوصف (al-wasf): A description or attribute attached to a noun that conditions the ruling according to the Hanafi school, but does not necessarily imply the opposite when absent (mafhūm al-mukhālafa).
التعليق بالشرط (al-ta‘līq bi al-shart): Suspending a ruling upon the occurrence of a condition. Here, the passage explains that a description (wasf) is analogous to a condition in ta‘līq.
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhūm al-mukhālafa): The implied opposite meaning: that the absence of a restriction negates the ruling. The Hanafis do not accept this as a proof (ḥujja) in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is marrying a Kitābī (Jewish or Christian) slave woman permissible despite the Quranic verse stating 'from your believing slave girls'?
A) Because the verse about believing slave girls is abrogated.
B) Because the restriction to 'believing' is for recommendation (istihbāb), not a condition, and the general verses permit marriage to women and slave women.
C) Because the Kitābī woman is not a slave.
D) Because the hadith allows it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a description in a text affirms the ruling when present but does not negate it when absent; the ruling for absent cases is derived from general proofs.

Exception (Istithnā') as a Form of Taghayyur
Defines exception (istithnā') as speaking of the remainder after exclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of istithnā' and apply it to identify the legal effect of an exception in a general statement.

Core Idea
Exception treats the excluded part as unspoken; only the remainder bears the ruling.

The Hanafi school defines exception (istithnā') as a linguistic operation that changes the scope of a general statement. When a speaker says 'ten except three', the legal effect is as if only 'seven' was uttered. This concept is fundamental to understanding how general texts (amm) are restricted in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms
Locate the key terms in the definition: al-istithnā', al-bāqī, al-thunyā, and al-mustathnā. Understand the relationship between them.
al-mustathnā is the excluded part, al-bāqī is the remainder.
2
Understand the Hanafi analogy
The Hanafis compare istithnā' to ghāya (limit). In both cases, the ruling is negated beyond the limit or for the excluded part due to absence of proof.
This analogy helps justify why the excluded part has no ruling.
3
Apply to an example
Take the statement 'He owes me ten except three.' Apply the definition: the remainder is seven, so the legal effect is a debt of seven.
The excluded three are treated as if never mentioned.
4
Recognize the scope
Note that istithnā' is a form of taghayyur (change) in speech, meaning it modifies the apparent meaning of the original statement.
This distinguishes it from other types of bayān (explanation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن صور بيان التغيير الاستثناء ذهب أصحابنا إلى أن الاستثناء تكلم بالباقي بعد الثنيا كأنه لم يتكلم بالمستثنى. (4) قوله: [بالباقي] ففي قوله: «له علي عشرة إلا ثلاثة» صدر الكلام «عشرة» والمستثنى «ثلاثة» والباقي في صدر الكلام بعد المستثنى سبعة، فكأنه تكلّم بسبعة وقال له: «علي سبعة». (5) قوله: [بعد الثنيا] أي: بعد الاستثناء وينعدم الحكم في المستثنى لعدم الدليل الموجب له مع صورة التكلّم به منزلة الغاية، فإنّ الحكم ينعدم فيما وراء الغاية لعدم الدليل الموجب له؛ لأنّ الغاية توجب نفي الحكم فيما وراءها.
Among the forms of explanation of change: exception (istithnā'). Our companions (the Hanafis) held that exception is speaking of the remainder after the exclusion, as if he had not spoken the excluded part. (4) Regarding 'of the remainder', in his statement 'He owes me ten except three', the opening of the speech is 'ten', the excluded is 'three', and the remainder in the opening of the speech after the exclusion is seven. So it is as if he spoke of seven and said: 'He owes me seven.' (5) Regarding 'after the exclusion', i.e., after the exception, and the ruling is absent for the excluded part due to the absence of a proof that would necessitate it, despite the form of speaking it, similar to the limit (ghāya). For the ruling is absent beyond the limit due to the absence of a proof necessitating it, because the limit entails negation of the ruling beyond it.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a definition of istithnā' (exception) from the Hanafi perspective. It states that when a speaker makes an exception, the legal effect is as if only the remaining part of the statement (after subtracting the excluded) was uttered. For example, saying 'I owe ten except three' is treated as if the speaker said 'I owe seven'. The exception does not negate the original statement entirely; rather, it limits it. The commentary explains that the excluded part (mustathnā) has no ruling because no proof (dalīl) establishes it, analogous to a limit (ghāya) in Islamic law. The passage establishes this as one type of 'taghyīr'—a change in the wording or interpretation of a legal text.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithnā’): A linguistic operation where the speaker makes an exception from a general statement, implying that the ruling applies only to the remainder after the exclusion.
الثنيا (al-thunyā): Synonym for exception (istithnā’); the act of excluding something.
الباقي (al-bāqī): The remainder of the number or quantity after the exception is subtracted.
الغاية (al-ghāya): A limit or endpoint in speech, analogous to exception in that the ruling is negated beyond it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, when someone says 'I owe you ten dirhams except three', what is the legal effect?
A) The debt is entirely negated because the exception makes the statement invalid.
B) The debt is seven dirhams, as if he only said 'I owe you seven'.
C) The debt is ten dirhams, and the exception is ignored.
D) The debt is three dirhams, as that is the excluded amount.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, exception (istithnā') is defined as speaking of the remainder after exclusion; the excluded part is treated as unspoken, and no ruling applies to it without separate proof.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Attribute and Exception in General Texts
Explains two forms of bayan al-taghyir with Hanafi-Shafi'i disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze how Hanafi and Shafi'i usul principles lead to different rulings on a text containing an attribute or an exception, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah) of the difference.

Core Idea
Exception in Hanafi usul removes the excepted from the ruling; in Shafi'i, it opposes the general cause.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, the author presents two forms of bayan al-taghyir (clarification by modification): attribute (wasf) and exception (istithna). These linguistic tools change the apparent scope of a general command, and the schools differ on how they operate. By working through the example of the hadith prohibiting food exchange except equally, you will see how the same text yields a different ruling in each school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two forms of taghyir
The passage opens by presenting the Shafi'i view on attribute (wasf) restricting a ruling, then moves to exception (istithna). First, locate the example of the attribute 'believing' in the Quranic verse. Then note how the author transitions to exception as another form.
The text begins with al-Shafi'i's claim that an attribute like 'believing' conditions the ruling.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i view on exception
According to al-Shafi'i, the beginning of a statement (sadr al-kalam) creates a cause (illah) for the entire ruling. The exception then opposes that cause only for the excepted part, leaving the rest under the original ruling. See how he applies this to the hadith: the prohibition is absolute, and only equal exchange is exempted.
This leads to the prohibition of selling a handful for two handfuls.
3
Examine the Hanafi counter-view
The Hanafi school holds that exception is a form of 'speaking of the remainder' (al-takallum bil-baqi). The excepted part is removed entirely from the scope of the ruling. In the hadith, the exception excludes all cases where equality is not achieved, so the prohibition only applies to exchanges where equality is possible but absent.
Thus selling a handful for two handfuls is not prohibited because equality cannot be achieved in such a small quantity.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of this usul difference is that for a sale of a small quantity like a handful of wheat for two handfuls, Hanafis allow it, while Shafi'is prohibit it. This illustrates how the same nas can generate opposing rulings based on the interpretive principle applied to the exception.
The passage explicitly states this result.
5
Derive the usul principle
The Hanafi view on istithna is a corollary of their general principle that general commands (amm) are definitive (qat'i) and can only be restricted by a specific proof. The exception itself is that proof. The Shafi'i view treats the exception as a separate clause that does not alter the initial general cause but creates an exemption.
This distinction is rooted in the nature of exception as either linguistic removal or permissive opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما بيان التغيير
قال الشافعي رحمه الله: لا يجوز نكاح الأمة الكتابية؛ لأن النص رتب الحكم على أمة مؤمنة لقوله تعالى: {مِن فَتَيَاتِكُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَات} [النساء: 25] فيتقيد بالمؤمنة فيمتنع الحكم عند عدم الوصف فلا يجوز نكاح الأمة الكتابية.
ومن صور بيان التغيير الاستثناء ذهب أصحابنا إلى أن الاستثناء تكلم بالباقي بعد الثنيا كأنه لم يتكلم إلا بما بقي وعنده صدر الكلام ينعقد علة لوجوب الكل إلا أن الاستثناء يمنعها من العمل بمنزلة عدم الشرط في باب التعليق، ومثال هذا في قوله عليه السلام لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام إلا سواء بسواء فعند الشافعي رحمه الله صدر الكلام انعقد علة لحرمة بيع الطعام بالطعام على الإطلاق، وخرج عن هذه الجملة صورة المساواة بالاستثناء فبقي الباقي تحت الإطلاق، ونتيجة هذا حرمة بيع الحفنة من الطعام بحفنتين منه، وعندنا الحفنة لا يدخل تحت النص، لأن المراد بالمنهي يتقيّد بصورة بيع يتمكن بالحفنتين.
Section: Regarding clarification of modification. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is not permissible to marry a Kitabiyya slave woman because the text attached the ruling to a believing slave woman by His statement: 'from your believing slave-girls' (al-Nisa 4:25). So it is restricted to the believing one, and the ruling is prevented when the attribute is absent, so it is not permissible to marry the Kitabiyya slave woman. Among the forms of clarification of modification is exception. Our school holds that exception is speaking of the remainder after exclusion, as if he did not speak except what remains. According to him (al-Shafi'i), the beginning of the statement constitutes a cause for the obligation of the whole, but the exception prevents it from operating, akin to the absence of a condition in conditional clauses. An example is in his statement (peace be upon him): 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal.' According to al-Shafi'i, the beginning of the statement constitutes a cause for the prohibition of selling food for food in absolute terms, and the form of equality is excluded from this sentence by the exception, so the remainder falls under the absolute ruling. The result is the prohibition of selling a handful of food for two handfuls. According to us, the handful is not included under the text because the intended prohibition is restricted to a form of sale in which equality can be achieved with two handfuls.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from al-Shashi's Usul explains the concept of bayan al-taghyir (clarification of modification), which occurs when a text specifies a ruling with an attribute or an exception, thereby altering the apparent generality. The author first presents the Shafi'i view: when an attribute like 'believing' is attached to the subject (slave woman), the ruling (permissibility of marriage) is tied to that attribute. Thus, according to al-Shafi'i, the absence of the attribute (i.e., the woman being non-believing) negates the ruling. The Hanafi response, not fully detailed here but implied, is that the attribute is for recommendation (istihbab) not condition, as the general permission to marry slave women applies unless a specific prohibition exists. The passage then turns to exception (istithna) as another form of taghyir. The Hanafi school (as expressed by 'أصحابنا') holds that an exception effectively removes the excepted part from the original ruling, so that the speaker is considered to have only said the remainder. For example, in the hadith 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal,' the Hanafis interpret the exception as restricting the prohibition to cases where equality is not achieved, so selling a handful for two handfuls is not covered because the exception removes the scenario of inequality. Al-Shafi'i, however, views the exception as a separate clause that opposes the general cause, resulting in a prohibition of all food-for-food sales except when equality is present. Thus, for al-Shafi'i, selling a handful for two handfuls is prohibited because it falls under the absolute prohibition, while the exception only allows equal exchanges. The passage concludes by noting that the Hanafi view limits the prohibited sale to those where the parties can actually measure equality, excluding small quantities. This illustrates how the same text can yield different rulings based on the usul principle applied.

Key Terms
الوصف (al-wasf): An attribute that restricts the ruling's application, as in 'believing' restricting the ruling of marrying slave women.
الاستثناء (al-istithna): An exception that removes the excepted item from the scope of the ruling; Hanafis view it as linguistic removal, Shafi'is as permissive opposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of an exception in a general command?
A) The excepted part is removed from the ruling, and the remaining statement applies as if the exception was never said.
B) The exception creates a separate ruling that overrides the general command only for the excepted case.
C) The general command remains valid for all cases, but the exception allows a concession.
D) The exception nullifies the entire general command.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ fundamentally on whether exception removes the excepted from the ruling (Hanafi) or merely opposes the general cause (Shafi'i), leading to distinct practical rulings on the same text.

How Exception Modifies a Causal Ruling: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Analysis of exception's effect on causality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on how exception (istithna') modifies a causal ruling, and apply the difference to a concrete fiqh example.

Core Idea
Exception nullifies the cause for the excluded part; it does not merely limit the ruling.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, we examine a fundamental difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal effect of an exception (istithna') in a causal statement. Using the hadith "Do not sell food for food except equal for equal," the author demonstrates how the two schools derive different rulings for a sale of unequal quantities that cannot be precisely measured. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school treats the relationship between a general cause ('illah) and its exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What is the effect of an exception (istithna') on the causal force of the preceding statement? Does it nullify the cause for the excluded case or merely limit the ruling?
The issue is about the operation of the 'illah after exception.
2
State the Hanafi position
The exception prevents the cause from operating on the excluded case entirely. The statement is interpreted as if the excepted part was never included in the causal scope.
Analogy: 'So-and-so owes me one thousand except one hundred' means he owes nine hundred.
3
State the Shafi'i position
The exception only excludes the specified case from the ruling, while the cause remains in effect for all other cases. The statement is interpreted as the cause applying generally except for the excluded instance.
Analogy: The exception is like takhsis of a general term.
4
Examine the proofs
Hanafi proof: analogy with conditional suspension (ta'liq) – just as a missing condition prevents the cause from working, an exception prevents the cause for the excluded case. Shafi'i proof: the cause is explicit and remains valid, only the ruling is lifted for the exception.
Both rely on linguistic and logical analysis of the structure 'A except B'.
5
Apply to the fiqh example
The hadith: 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal.' Hanafi: prohibition only applies to sales where equality can be measured (standard measures). Selling a handful (non-standard) for two handfuls is not covered, thus permissible. Shafi'i: prohibition covers any unequal sale, including handful for two handfuls, since they are not equal.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear in this case.

The little is what does not fall under measurement, and the much is what falls under it, because 'food' is a generic noun defined by 'al' so it includes all. (12) (5) His statement: [does not fall under the text, which is his statement, peace be upon him: 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal.' This, i.e. its not falling under the text is established because the prohibition is leaving equality in selling much for much, not in selling absolute; because the prohibition only occurs in what the servant is able to do, lest it lead to prohibition of the incapable, which is ugly. So the intended meaning is that the prohibited sale is restricted to a form in which the servant can establish equality and disparity, which is selling much; because the equalizer is... (12) ... (Page 199 continuation)... 'on' (12) i.e. that sale. (12) This prohibition. (12) Section: On explanation of modification. Like selling a handful for two handfuls. (12) The servant's ability to establish equality and disparity in it, lest it lead to prohibition of the incapable. So what does not fall under the equalizing standard is outside the purport of the hadith. And examples of the modification of the measure and weight. (12) i.e. the speaker. (12) The modification is when he says: 'So-and-so owes me one thousand as a trust.' His statement 'owes' indicates obligation... (12) i.e. the speaker. (12) dirham. (12) To distinguish the thousand. (12) i.e. you gave me in salam. (12) And it is by his saying 'trust' he changed it to custody, and his saying 'you gave me' or 'you lent me' (12) i.e. the mentioned dirhams with a thousand. (12) From the category of modification. (12) ... a thousand, so not... (12) unlike the good coins. (12) I received it from the category of modification, and likewise if he said: 'So-and-so owes me a thousand bad dirhams.' ... Measurement by consensus, so what does not fall under measurement the servant cannot establish equality and leave it, so it is not included under the prohibition, as was said. (12) (1) His statement: [Lest it lead to prohibition of the incapable... etc. And it is ugly, and equality is only established by the equalizing standard. The equalizing standard in the explanation for food is measurement by consensus, and by the evidence of his statement, peace be upon him: 'measure for measure,' and by custom, for food is not sold customarily except measure for measure, and by legal effect, for damaging less than the like in food does not obligate the like but obligates the value due to loss of the equalizer. So the prohibition is leaving equality in selling much food for much food, not in absolute selling, as in al-Ma'dan. (12) (2) His statement: [is outside... etc.] For its meaning is: Do not sell food in any case except in the case of equality. So if the two countervalues are equal, then sell. (12) (3) His statement: [changed it to custody] i.e. the word 'owes' from obligation, i.e. custody. (12) So the obligation in the dhimmah was understood from 'owes,' and he removed it to the obligation of custody, i.e. for its custody, not for its obligation. So it is a transfer either to metonymy or ellipsis. (12) (4) His statement: [From the category of modification, for giving is not completed except by taking possession, so it is the reality of delivery, and a loan is taking an immediate for a deferred, so acknowledging them is an acknowledgment of taking possession in reality, except that it is possible that by them is meant merely the contract metaphorically; because 'islaf' indicates a salam contract and 'i'ta' indicates a gift contract. Hence, if he said: 'I gave you this reward' and the other said: 'I accepted,' it is a gift, so it is valid on condition of continuity, not separation, as in al-Ma'dan. (12) (5) His statement: [owes... etc.] For his statement 'owes one thousand' obligates good coins in appearance, because transactions only occur with good coins, not with bad except rarely, so intending the bad is like a metaphor from reality. (12)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul al-fiqh principle of how an exception (istithna') interacts with a causal statement ('illa). The specific example is the hadith: 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal.' The passage contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the exception prevents the first part of the statement from being a cause for the prohibition over the excluded case. In other words, the prohibition applies only to sales where the two quantities can be compared and equality or disparity established. Therefore, selling a handful (which is not a standard measure) for two handfuls is not covered by the hadith and is permissible. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the first part remains a cause for prohibition in general, and the exception merely excludes equality; thus, any unequal sale is prohibited, including a handful for two handfuls because they are not equal. The passage also draws an analogy with the statement 'So-and-so owes me one thousand except one hundred,' where Abu Hanifa interprets it as owing nine hundred (the exception nullifies the effect of the thousand), while al-Shafi'i interprets it as owing one thousand minus one hundred (the thousand remains binding except for the hundred). The commentary from al-Ma'dan explains that the equalizing standard for food is measurement by volume (kil) by consensus, hadith, and custom, so small quantities that are not measured fall outside the prohibition. Additional examples of 'modification' (taghyir) include changing the meaning of 'owes' by adding 'trust' (changing from obligation to custody) or changing the type of currency (good vs. bad coins).

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā’): Exception; a particle (e.g., 'illa) that excludes part of a general statement from the ruling.
علة (‘illah): The effective cause or ratio legis that triggers a ruling.
تغيير (taghyīr): Modification; changing the apparent meaning of a statement by adding a clause that alters its legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, why is selling a handful of food for two handfuls not prohibited by the hadith 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal'?
A) Because the handful is less than the standard measure, so the exception does not apply.
B) Because the prohibition only applies to sales where equality can be measured, and a handful is not a standard measure.
C) Because the hadith has been abrogated.
D) Because the exception (except equal for equal) allows any unequal sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an exception (istithna') does not merely limit the ruling; it prevents the causal statement from applying to the excepted case altogether.

Bayān al-Taġyīr: Connected vs. Disconnected Modification
Defines Bayān al-Taġyīr and its validity condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul requires bayān al-taġyīr to be connected, and apply the rule to distinguish valid from invalid modifications.

Core Idea
A modifying statement must be connected; otherwise it amounts to impermissible naskh.

This lesson introduces the crucial concept of bayān al-taġyīr (statement of modification). The Hanafi school holds that such statements, like exceptions and conditions, are only valid when attached directly to the original speech. We will explore the rational and transmitted evidence behind this rule, and the significant difference it makes in practice.

Guided Path
1
Define the Term
Identify what bayān al-taġyīr means: a statement that modifies the original speech, such as a condition or exception.
The modification changes the ruling of the original statement.
2
State the Ruling
The passage rules that modification is valid when connected (mawsulan) and invalid when disconnected (mafsulan).
This is the core ruling of the lesson.
3
Examine the Rational Proof
Why must it be connected? Because conditions and exceptions are dependent clauses; if disconnected, they would contradict the established effect of the initial speech, acting as abrogation (naskh), which is impermissible for humans.
Connectedness prevents naskh by an individual.
4
Analyze the Transmitted Proof
The Prophet's hadith: 'Whoever takes an oath and then sees something better, let him expiate his oath and do the better thing.' This shows that expiation is the only remedy for an oath; a delayed exception is not allowed.
If delayed exception were valid, it would also be a remedy without expiation.
5
Evaluate the Counter-argument
The view attributed to Ibn Abbas that a delayed exception is valid is rejected because the report is unreliable. Even if reliable, it is interpreted as an inner intention accepted only in private conscience, not judicially.
The Hanafi position is adopted by the majority and relied upon.

عن
(۳) قوله فتصح بشرط الوصل] أي: إن كان من جملة بيان التغيير فتصح موصولاً لا مفصولاً، وعلى هذا أجمع الفقهاء لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من حلف على يمين ورأي غيرها خيراً منها فليكفّر يمينه ثُمّ ليأت بالذي هو خير» الحديث. جعل مخلص اليمين هو الكفّارة ولو صح الاستثناء متراخيــــاً لجعله مخلصاً أيضاً بأن يقول: «الآن إن شاء الله تعالى ويبطل اليمين ولا يجب الكفّارة، وعن ابن عباس الله تعالى عنه أنه يصح مفصولاً أيضاً لما روي أنه عليه السلام قال: «لأَغْزُوَنَّ قُرَيْشًا ثُمَّ قَالَ بَعْدَ سَنَة إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالى وهذا أي: النقل عن ابن عباس غير صحيح عندنا ولو صح فلعل مراده أنه إذا نوى أجل الاستثناء عند التلفظ ثُمّ أظهر نيته بعد التلفّظ فيقبل قوله فيما نواه ديانةً فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى وذهبه أنّ ما يقبل فيه قول العبد ديانةً يقبل فيه قوله ظاهراً، وروي أنه قال أبو جعفر بن منصور الذي كان من الخلفاء العباسية أبي حنيفة رحمه الله : لم خالفت جدّي أي: ابن عباس في عدم صحته الاستثناء متراخياً؟ فقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : لو صح ذلك بارك الله في بيعتك أي: يقول الناس: «الآن إن شاء الله تعالى» فتنتقض بيعتك فتحيّر أبو جعفر وسكت وألحق ما قال به الجمهور وعليه الاعتماد والله أعلم، كذا في "الحصول". ١٢
Chapter: As for the statement of modification – the agreement of the jurists, may Allah elevate them, indeed it is the statement of matters of modification. The ruling of the statement of modification is that it is valid when connected and not valid when disconnected. Then after this are matters concerning validity and invalidity from the Hanafis. Those matters are the ones disputed. ... (footnotes) ...
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Usul al-Shashi defines Bayān al-Taġyīr (statement of modification) and its ruling. The author states that the Hanafi jurists agree that a modifying statement, such as a condition or exception, is valid only if it is connected to the original speech (mawsulan) and invalid if disconnected (mafsulan). The commentary explains the reasoning: conditions and exceptions are dependent clauses that have no independent meaning, so they must be linked. If disconnected, they would contradict the established ruling of the initial statement, effectively acting as an abrogation (naskh), which is not permissible for humans. The passage also discusses a dispute attributed to Ibn Abbas, who reportedly allowed delayed exception, citing a hadith about the Prophet delaying 'insha'Allah' from his oath. The Hanafi response is that this report is unreliable, and even if reliable, it is interpreted as an intention of the exception at the time of utterance which is later expressed – accepted only in the private conscience (diyānah), not judicially. The story of Abu Hanifa’s interaction with Caliph Abu Jaʿfar al-Mansur reinforces the Hanafi position to prevent people from nullifying oaths by adding later exceptions.

Key Terms
بيان التغيير (Bayān al-Taġyīr): A statement that modifies the original speech, such as a condition or exception, which must be connected to be valid.
موصول (Mawṣūl): Connected: the modifying statement is attached directly to the original statement without a separation.
مفصول (Mafṣūl): Disconnected: the modifying statement is separated from the original statement by time or speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a disconnected modifying statement (مفصول) invalid according to Hanafi usul?
A) Because it contradicts consensus (ijma).
B) Because it would constitute abrogation (naskh) by a human, which is not permitted.
C) Because the original statement was incomplete.
D) Because the Prophet forbade delayed speech.

Key Takeaway
Remember: In Hanafi usul, a modifying statement is valid only when connected; a disconnected modification is void because it amounts to forbidden naskh.

Intercourse as Specification: Divorce vs Freeing
Comparison of intercourse as specifying act in ambiguous freeing and divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Hanifa's distinction between ambiguous divorce and ambiguous freeing regarding the specifying effect of intercourse, and apply the principle of maqasid (objectives) to determine specification.

Core Idea
Intercourse specifies in ambiguous divorce due to natural aversion, but not in ambiguous freeing due to dual avenues of permissibility.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi presents a key dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on whether a physical act (intercourse) can resolve ambiguity in legal statements. The analysis hinges on understanding the underlying objectives (maqasid) of marriage versus slave ownership. By examining the reasoning, you will learn how Hanafi usul uses contextual factors to interpret actions as legal specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two ambiguous scenarios
The lesson compares two cases: (1) a man says to his two wives 'One of you is divorced' and then has intercourse with one; (2) a man says to his two female slaves 'One of you is free' and then has intercourse with one. Identify the ambiguity in each.
In both, the statement is ambiguous (mubham), and the action (intercourse) is examined for specifying effect.
2
State the ruling in divorce
According to the text, intercourse in the divorce case specifies the woman not violated as the divorced one. Why? Because natural aversion makes intercourse with a divorced woman unlikely, so violating one indicates she is the non-divorced wife.
The principle: if an action is unlikely with a certain legal status, it becomes a strong indicator of intention.
3
State the ruling in freeing and the dispute
Abu Hanifa says intercourse does NOT specify in freeing. The Sahibayn say it does. Understand both positions before diving into reasoning.
The source uses 'bikhilaf al-wati' to signal the exception.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning (talil)
Abu Hanifa argues that the permissibility of intercourse with a female slave can arise from either ownership (milk al-yamin) or marriage after emancipation. Thus, intercourse does not determine which path is operative. In divorce, only one path (remaining marriage) is plausible because the divorced woman is undesirable for a new marriage.
The key distinction is the number of possible legal avenues for permissibility: one in divorce, two in freeing.
5
Apply the maqasid principle
Abu Hanifa further notes that the primary objective of marriage is offspring, so intercourse indicates intent to preserve the marriage. With a slave woman, the objective is gratification, not offspring, so intercourse does not indicate intent to preserve ownership.
This shows how maqasid (objectives) inform the interpretation of acts as specifying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما بيان الضرورة في الأخرى " بخلاف الوطئ في العتق المبهم عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن حل الوطئ في الملك والنكاح. الإماء يثبت بطريقين فلا يتعيّن جهة الملك باعتبار حل الوطئ. (۱) قوله: [في الأخرى... إلخ] دون الموطوءة؛ لأنّ الظاهر من حال المسلم أن يجتنب عن وطئ المطلقة البائنة وإذا كان الطلاق رجعيًّا لا يكون بيانا لاحتمال الرجعة بالوطئ وهو الظاهر؛ لأنّ الشرع دعا إليه على سبيل الاستحباب، والظاهر من حال المسلم الإجابة، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (۲) قوله: [في الأخرى التى لم يطأها؛ لأنّ الظاهر أنه لايطأ المطلقة وإن كانت رجعية لنفور الطبيعة، فيكون وطي إحداهما بياناً للمطلقة، كذا في "المنهاج". (۳) قوله: [بخلاف الوطئ... إلخ] بأن كانت له أمتان، فقال: «إحدكما حرّة» ثُمّ وطئ إحدهما، فإنه ليس ببيان العتق في الأخرى وهذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله؛ لأنّ حلّ الوطئ في الإماء يثبت بطريقين: أحدهما بطريق المملوكية، وثانيهما بطريق أنها نكحت بعد الإعتاق، وعندهما لا فرق بين الوطئ في العتق المبهم والطلاق المبهم، والفرق لأبي حنيفة أن المقصود الأصلي من النكاح الولد وقصد الولد بالوطئ يدل على استبقاء الملك في الموطوءة وصيانة للولد أمّا الأمة فالمقصود من وطئها قضاء الشهوة دون الولد فلا يدل وطئها على استبقاء الملك في الأمة الموطوءة، كذا في كتب الأصول. ١٢ (٤) قوله: [فلا يتعيّن... إلخ] لا يقال: الحلّ في المنكوحة أيضاً بطرقين: أحدهما بطريق الملك الأوّل، وثانيهما بطريق النكاح الجديد، لأنا نقول: الظاهر من حال المطلقة عدم النكاح لفوات الرغبة عنها فكان الطريق واحداً وهو بقاء النكاح الأوّل، وأما الأمة ففيها طريقان: طريق ملك اليمين وطريق ملك النكاح، أو نكاحها مرغوب فيه لزوال الرقّ عنها، هذا خلاصة الكتب. ١٢
Chapter: And as for clarification of necessity in the other [case]." Contrary to intercourse in ambiguous freeing according to Abu Hanifa; because the permissibility of intercourse is through ownership and marriage. Female slaves are established by two paths, so the avenue of ownership is not determined by considering the permissibility of intercourse. (1) He said: [in the other... etc.] meaning the one not violated; because the apparent state of a Muslim is to avoid intercourse with a divorced woman in a final divorce, and if the divorce is revocable, it is not a specification due to the possibility of revocation by intercourse, which is apparent because the Law encourages it as recommended, and the apparent state of a Muslim is to respond. Thus in al-Ma'din. (2) He said: [in the other whom he has not violated; because it is apparent that he does not have intercourse with a divorced woman even if revocable due to natural aversion, so his intercourse with one of them is a specification of the divorced one. Thus in al-Minhaj. (3) He said: [Contrary to intercourse... etc.] As if he had two female slaves and said, 'One of you is free,' then had intercourse with one of them; it is not a specification of freeing the other according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because the permissibility of intercourse with slave women is established by two paths: one by way of ownership, and the second by way that she married after emancipation. According to them (the two companions), there is no difference between intercourse in ambiguous freeing and ambiguous divorce. The difference for Abu Hanifa is that the primary objective of marriage is offspring, and the intention of offspring through intercourse indicates the preservation of ownership in the violated woman and protection of the child. As for the female slave, the objective of intercourse is fulfilling desire without offspring, so intercourse does not indicate preservation of ownership in the violated slave woman. Thus in the books of usul. (4) He said: [So it is not determined... etc.] It may not be said: The permissibility in the married woman is also by two paths: one by way of the first marriage, and the second by way of a new marriage. For we say: The apparent state of the divorced woman is lack of marriage due to loss of desire for her, so the path is one: the remaining of the first marriage. As for the female slave, there are two paths: the path of right-hand ownership and the path of marriage ownership, or her marriage is desirable due to removal of slavery. This is the summary of the books.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This is a usul dispute passage dealing with the principle of specification (bayan) through action when a statement is ambiguous (mubham). The specific issue is whether intercourse (wat') by a man who has ambiguously divorced one of his wives or ambiguously freed one of his female slaves serves to specify which one is intended. The matn begins by stating that in the case of ambiguous divorce, if the husband has intercourse with one of them, it specifies the divorced woman, contrary to the case of ambiguous freeing of a female slave. The commentator explains that in divorce, it is the natural aversion to a divorced woman that makes intercourse with her improbable, so if he does have intercourse, it indicates she is not the divorced one, thus specifying the other. However, in freeing, according to Abu Hanifa, intercourse does not specify because the permissibility of intercourse with a female slave can be due to either ownership (milk al-yamin) or marriage (milk al-nikah) after emancipation. Since both possibilities remain, intercourse does not determine which one was freed. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree and hold that intercourse specifies in both cases. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is based on the primary objectives: in marriage, the goal is offspring, so intercourse indicates a desire to preserve the marriage; in female slavery, the goal is gratification, so intercourse does not indicate which avenue is operative. The passage ends with a rebuttal to a potential objection and concludes with the Hanafi position. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it is a core usul principle.

Key Terms
عتق مبهم (itq mubham): An ambiguous freeing where one of multiple slaves is declared free without specification.
طلاق مبهم (talaq mubham): An ambiguous divorce where one of multiple wives is divorced without specification.
وطء (wat'): Sexual intercourse; used here as a potential specifying act (bayan bil-fi'l).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does intercourse not specify the ambiguous freeing of a female slave?
A) Because intercourse is prohibited with a slave woman
B) Because the permissibility of intercourse can be through either ownership or marriage
C) Because the female slave cannot be freed by intercourse
D) Because the owner's intention is always unknown

Key Takeaway
Intercourse specifies in ambiguous divorce due to natural aversion and unidirectional possibility, but not in ambiguous freeing due to dual avenues of permissibility; context and maqasid drive the Hanafi distinction.
