Bayan al-'Atf: Clarification by Conjunction in Hanafi Usul
Defining clarification by conjunction and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of clarificatory conjunction to determine when a conjunction resolves an ambiguous term, identify the required conditions (mithli and debt-suitability), and compare the positions of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Conjunction clarifies an ambiguous term only when the conjoined item is fungible and debt-suitable; Abu Yusuf extends it to all items.

In legal texts, ambiguous terms often require clarification. The Hanafi school recognizes that conjoining (atf) a specific item to a general term can remove that ambiguity, but only under certain conditions. This lesson unpacks the rule of bayan al-'atf, its limitations, and the scholarly differences surrounding it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the principle: conjoining a specific item to an ambiguous general term clarifies that the general refers to the genus of the specific item.
This is the core claim: the conjunction itself serves as bayan.
2
Apply the condition
Check if the conjoined item is mithli (fungible, measurable/weighable) and suitable as a debt in the dhimma. If yes, the rule applies. If not, the general remains ambiguous (per the majority of Hanafis).
Non-mithli items like sheep or unique garments do not trigger clarification.
3
Test with examples from the text
Work through the examples: 'a hundred and a qafiz of wheat' (clarifies), 'a hundred and three dirhams' (clarifies), 'a hundred and a sheep' (does not clarify per majority, but Abu Yusuf disagrees).
Notice the pattern: when the conjoined item is single and mithli, it clarifies.
4
Analyze the intra- and inter-madhhab disputes
Compare Abu Yusuf's view (extends clarification to non-mithli because of brevity) with the majority Hanafi view, and contrast with al-Shafi'i's position (no automatic clarification; interpretation from context).
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: practical effect on contracts.

فصل وأما بيان العطف فمثل أن تعطف مكيلا أو موزونا على جملة مجملة يكون ذلك بيانا للجملة المجملة مثاله إذا قال: «لفلان علي مئة وقفيز حنطة كان العطف بمنزلة البيان أن الكل من ذلك أي المئة والدرهم الواحد. وكذا لو قال: «مئة وثلاثة أثواب» أو «مئة وثلاثة دراهم» أو «مئة وثلاثة أعبد فإنه بيان أنّ المئة من ذلك الجنس بمنزلة قوله: «أحد وعشرون درهما بخلاف قوله: «مئة وثوب» أو «مئة وشاة» حيث لا يكون ذلك بيانا للمئة، واختص ذلك في عطف الواحد بما يصلح دينا في الذمة من المثلي كالمكيل والموزون، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : يكون بيانا في «مئة وشاة» و «مئة وثوب» نظرا إلى الاختصار من التعاطف. خلافا للشافعي فعنده يطلب تفسيره من قائد.
Section: As for clarification by conjunction, it is like when you conjoin a measurable or weighable thing to a general ambiguous sentence – that becomes a clarification of the ambiguous sentence. Example: if he says, 'So-and-so owes me a hundred [unclear] and a qafiz of wheat', the conjunction serves as clarification that the whole is of that [kind] – i.e., the hundred and the one dirham. Similarly, if he says, 'a hundred and three garments' or 'a hundred and three dirhams' or 'a hundred and three slaves', then it is clarification that the hundred is from that genus, like his statement, 'twenty-one dirhams'. Unlike his statement, 'a hundred and a garment' or 'a hundred and a sheep' where that is not a clarification of the hundred. And that is specific to the conjunction of a single item that is suitable as a debt in the dhimmah from the mithli category, such as measurable and weighable items. Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: It is clarification in 'a hundred and a sheep' and 'a hundred and a garment' considering the abbreviation from conjunction. Contrary to al-Shafi'i, who holds that its interpretation is sought from the context.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage explains 'clarification by conjunction' (bayan al-'atf). The principle is: when a specific item (e.g., 'a qafiz of wheat') is conjoined to an ambiguous general term (e.g., 'a hundred'), the conjunction clarifies that the general term belongs to the same genus as the specific item. Examples: 'a hundred and three dirhams' clarifies that the hundred is dirhams. However, this only applies when the conjoined item is suitable as a debt in the dhimma and is a mithli (fungible) like measurable/weighable items. 'A hundred and a sheep' does not clarify because a sheep is not mithli. Abu Yusuf held that even 'a hundred and a sheep' is clarificatory due to brevity. The text notes a difference with al-Shafi'i, who does not accept conjunction as automatic clarification; instead, the interpretation is sought from the context (qa'id). This shows that the Hanafi position grants greater interpretive weight to the conjunction itself.

Key Terms
بيان العطف (bayān al-‘aṭf): Clarification by conjunction: the legal principle that conjoining a specific item to an ambiguous general term clarifies the nature of the general term.
مثلي (mithlī): Fungible goods that are measured or weighed, like wheat or dirhams, which can be replaced by similar items.
ذمة (dhimmah): The legal personality or capacity of a person to incur debts and obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 'I owe you a hundred and a dirham'
B) 'I owe you a hundred and three garments'
C) 'I owe you a hundred and a sheep'
D) 'I owe you a hundred and two qafiz of wheat'

Key Takeaway
Bayan al-'atf clarifies an ambiguous term only when the conjoined item is mithli and debt-suitable; Abu Yusuf's broader view and al-Shafi'i's contrary opinion highlight the role of custom in Hanafi usul.

Bayan al-'Atf: How Conjunction Clarifies Ambiguous Nouns
Defines and exemplifies how conjunction clarifies an ambiguous preceding noun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that conjunction ('atf) serves as bayan only when the conjoined item is makil or mawzun suitable for dhimma debt, and evaluate Abu Yusuf's opposing view.

Core Idea
Conjunction clarifies ambiguity only when the second noun is a weight/volume item common in debts.

When someone says 'one hundred and a qafiz of wheat,' does the 'qafiz of wheat' clarify that the hundred is also wheat? Hanafi usul says yes, but only for certain items. This lesson explores how conjunction can serve as legal clarification (bayan), the conditions that make it valid, and an internal disagreement within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of bayan al-‘atf
Recognize that 'atf can explain an ambiguous (mujmal) noun when the conjoined item is a specific type of mithli: makil or mawzun.
The conjunction itself acts as the explicative (tafsir) for the first noun.
2
Analyze the condition: suitability for dhimma debt
Understand that the conjoined item must be something that can be owed in the dhimma – i.e., makil (volume) or mawzun (weight) – because these are standard in transactions.
Items like garments or sheep are not typically established in dhimma except in salam.
3
Examine the examples
Work through the examples given: 'one hundred and a qafiz of wheat' (bayan valid), 'one hundred and a garment' (invalid according to majority).
Note that numbers like 21 dirhams also show automatic clarity.
4
Consider Abu Yusuf's ikhtilaf
Evaluate Abu Yusuf's view that any conjoined item, even a garment or sheep, provides bayan based on the principle of brevity in conjunction.
The majority rejects this due to lack of custom for non-makil/mawzun items.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: if someone says 'one hundred and a sheep,' the majority says the hundred is still ambiguous (could be dirhams, etc.), while Abu Yusuf says it becomes a hundred sheep.
This affects debt claims and contractual interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما بيان العطف فمثل أن تعطف مكيلا أو موزونا على جملة مجملة يكون ذلك بيانا للجملة المجملة مثاله إذا قال: «لفلان علي مئة ومئة وقفيز حنطة» كان العطف بمنزلة البيان أن الكل من ذلك الجنس، وكذا لو قال: «مئة وثلاثة أثواب» أو «مئة وثلاثة دراهم» أو «مئة وثلاثة أعبد» فإنه بيان أنّ المئة من ذلك الجنس بمنزلة قوله: «أحد وعشرون درهما» بخلاف قوله: «مئة وثوب» أو «مئة وشاة» حيث لا يكون ذلك بيانا للمئة، واختص ذلك في عطف الواحد بما يصلح دينا في الذمة من المثلي كالمكيل والموزون، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : يكون بيانا في «مئة وشاة» و «مئة وثوب» نظرا إلى الاختصار من العطف على هذا الأصل. (۱) قوله على هذا الأصل] وهو كون المعطوف والمعطوف عليه بمنزلة شيء واحد؛ لأنّ الواو العاطفة للجمع كما في قوله: «مئة درهم، ولهما وجه الفرق بين المكيل والموزون وبين غيرهما أنّ العادة بحذف المفسر في المعطوف عليه والاكتفاء بذكر التفسير في المعطوف إنّما وجدت في المكيل والموزون بضرورة كثرة الكلام فيما كثر استعماله وكثرته فيما يثبت وينافي الذمة في عامة المعاملات وهو المقدّر بخلاف الثياب؛ لأنها لا تثبت في الذمة قرضاً ولا بيعاً إلا في السلم خاصةً، فلهذا لم يوجد الاكتفاء فيها، كذا في "المعدن" وشروح "البزدوي". ١٢
Section: And as for the explanation of conjunction, it is like when you conjoin something measured by volume (makil) or weight (mawzun) to an ambiguous (mujmal) sentence, that becomes an explanation for the ambiguous sentence. Its example: if he says, 'So-and-so owes me one hundred and one hundred and a qafiz of wheat,' the conjunction is in the position of an explanation that all is of that type. Likewise, if he says, 'one hundred and three garments,' or 'one hundred and three dirhams,' or 'one hundred and three slaves,' then it is an explanation that the hundred is of that type, similar to his saying 'twenty-one dirhams.' Contrary to his saying, 'one hundred and a garment' or 'one hundred and a sheep,' where that is not an explanation for the hundred. And that is specific to conjoining a single item that is suitable as a debt in the dhimma from among replaceable goods (mithli), like makil and mawzun. Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is an explanation in 'one hundred and a sheep' and 'one hundred and a garment,' considering brevity in conjunction upon this principle. (1) His saying 'upon this principle' means that the conjoined and the conjoined-to are like one thing, because the conjunction waw is for joining, as in his saying 'one hundred dirhams.' And they have a way to differentiate between makil/mawzun and others: the custom of omitting the explicative of the conjoined-to and being content with mentioning the explicative in the conjoined is found only in makil and mawzun due to the necessity of frequent speech in what is much used, and its abundance in what is established and affirmed in the dhimma in general transactions, which is quantified (muqaddar), unlike garments; because they are not established in the dhimma as a loan or sale except in salam specifically, so for this reason, being content with it is not found there. Thus in 'al-Ma'din' and the commentaries of 'al-Bazdawi.'
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi (with commentary) defines the concept of 'bayan al-‘atf' — explanation by conjunction. The author states that when a specific type of item (makil or mawzun) is conjoined to an ambiguous noun (mujmal or mubham), the conjunction itself acts as an explanation, clarifying the ambiguity. For example, if someone says 'one hundred and one hundred and a qafiz of wheat,' the conjunction of 'qafiz of wheat' explains that all the unspecified 'hundreds' are wheat. Similarly, if one says 'one hundred and three garments,' the three garments clarify that the hundred is also garments. However, this only applies when the conjoined item is a suitable debt in the dhimma, such as makil (volume) or mawzun (weight) — items that are homogenous and quantifiable. The commentary explains that customarily, people omit the explicative from the first (ambiguous) noun and rely on the explicative given in the conjoined item, but this custom is only established for makil/mawzun because these are frequently used in transactions and are quantified. In contrast, items like garments are not typically established in the dhimma except in salam contracts, so the same reasoning does not apply. Abu Yusuf disagreed, holding that even 'one hundred and a sheep' is explanatory, arguing for brevity. The passage thus highlights a key usul principle: 'atf can serve as bayan under specific conditions, and it also records an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
العطف (al-‘aṭf): Conjunction; linking one word or sentence to another using the letter waw or other conjunctions.
مجمل (mujmal): An ambiguous expression that requires clarification to determine its precise meaning.
مكيل (makīl): Items measured by volume, such as grains, that are typically quantified in transactions.
موزون (mawzūn): Items measured by weight, such as silver and gold, that are typically quantified in transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Whenever any item, regardless of type, is conjoined to an ambiguous number.
C) Only when the conjoined item is a garment or sheep.
D) Only when the number expressed is less than ten.

Key Takeaway
Conjunction clarifies an ambiguous number only when the conjoined item is a homogenous good (makil/mawzun) commonly used in debts.

Clarification vs. Substitution in Commutative Contracts
Explaining the Hanafi ruling on substitution in a statement about bad coins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a valid clarification (bayān) and an invalid substitution (tabdīl) in Hanafi usul, and apply the rule to a given contract scenario.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, any statement contradicting a contract's implied defect-free condition is a retraction, not a clarification.

When a party to a contract makes a statement that seems to clarify a prior obligation, we must determine whether it is a legitimate explanation or an attempt to retract. The Hanafi school has a nuanced position: if the statement contradicts the implied terms of a commutative contract, it is treated as an invalid substitution. This lesson explores the ruling through the example of 'bad coins' and the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios in the passage
The passage presents two cases: (1) saying 'they are bad coins' after acknowledging a debt, and (2) saying 'I did not receive her' after acknowledging a price for a slave-girl. Note the differing rulings between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn.
2
Understand the implied condition in commutative contracts
In a sale or debt contract, the default expectation is that the property is free from defects. The contract implicitly requires sound quality. This is the foundation for the ruling.
This is a rational (aqli) inference from the nature of exchange.
3
Analyze the positions: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa views any statement that contradicts the implied condition as a retraction (رجوع) which is invalid whether connected or disconnected. Sahibayn accept it as a clarification (بيان) if stated in the same breath because the original term 'thousand' is absolute and the specification of quality is a clarification of its nature.
The disagreement hinges on whether the apparent meaning of 'thousand' in a debt context implies good quality.
4
Apply the analogy to other cases
The passage analogizes claiming a defect to claiming a term in a debt or an option in a sale. Recognize how this qiyas strengthens Abu Hanifa's position.
Qiyas is used to extend the ruling to similar scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما بيان التبديل أي قوله هي زيوف. ١٢ «وهي زيوف» كان ذلك بيان التغيير عندهما فيصح موصولاً وهـو بيــــان بناء على ما زالته للمقصود في المقام . ١٢. (۲) وصلية. ١٢ التبديل عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله فلا يصح و إن وصل، ولو قال: «لفلان عليّ أي الجارية. ١٢. أي غير معلومة. ١٢ أي قوله لم أقبضها. ١٢ ألف من ثمن جارية باعنيها ولم أقبضها والجارية لا أثر لها كان ذلك بيان أي الجارية. ١٢ في الكثرة. ١٢ (۳) التبديل عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله؛ لأنّ الإقرار بلزوم الثمن إقرار بالقبض عند في ذمة المشتري. ١٢ بدون القبض. ١٢ هلاك المبيع؛ إذ لو هلك قبل القبض ينفسخ البيع فلا يبقى الثمن لازما . فعلم أن لزومه دال على القبض المقصود. ۱۲ (۱) قوله: [ عندهما ... إلخ ] ؛ لأنّ الألف مطلق عن قيد الجودة، لكنّ الظاهر منه في القرض والدين والثمن وأمثالها هو الجيد فهو تغيير له عن هذا الظاهر ، وأما عند ابي حنيفة وهو نسخ وتبديل فلا يصح موصولاً؛ لأنّ عقد المعاوضة مقتضاه السلامة عن العيب، والزيافة عيب فكان رجوعاً وهو لا يعتبر فيها لا موصولاً ولا مفصولاً. ۱۲ (۲) قوله: [فلا يصح وإن وصل] لأنّ عقد المعاوضة يقتضي وجوب المال بصفة السلامة عـــــن العيـــب، والزيافة عيب فكان رجوعاً والرجوع لا يعمل موصولاً ومفصولاً، وصار كدعوى الأجل في الدين ودعوى الخيار في البيع، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (۳) قوله: [إقرار بالقبض] فكان قوله : « لم أقبضها» رجوعاً بعد الإقرار بالقبض أو لزوم الثمن، والرجوع لا يصح موصولاً ولا مفصولاً . ۱۲
Section: And regarding the clarification of substitution — meaning his statement 'they are bad coins.' 'And they are bad coins' was a clarification of change according to the two (disciples), so it is valid as connected and it is a clarification based on what was removed for the objective in the context. (2) And as a connected statement? Substitution according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, is not valid even if connected. And if he said: 'So-and-so owes me...' meaning the slave-girl. Meaning unknown. Regarding abundance. (3) Substitution according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because acknowledging the necessity of the price is an acknowledgment of receipt while it is in the debtor's liability without receipt. Destruction of the sold item: for if it perishes before receipt, the sale is rescinded and the price does not remain binding. So it is known that its necessity indicates the intended receipt. (1) His statement: [according to them etc.] because the 'thousand' is unrestricted without the condition of quality, but the apparent from it in loans, debts, prices, and the like is good, so it is a change from this apparent. And according to Abu Hanifa, it is abrogation and substitution, so it is not valid as connected because a commutative contract requires freedom from defect, and bad quality is a defect, so it is a retraction, and it is not considered whether connected or disconnected. (2) His statement: [it is not valid even if connected] because a commutative contract necessitates obligation of the property with the quality of freedom from defect, and bad quality is a defect, so it is a retraction, and retraction does not work connected or disconnected, and it becomes like claiming a term in a debt or claiming an option in a sale. As in al-Ma'dan. (3) His statement: [acknowledgment of receipt] so his statement 'I did not receive her' is a retraction after acknowledgment of receipt or necessity of the price, and retraction is not valid whether connected or disconnected.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of a statement that clarifies or changes a prior commitment in the context of a contract. The matn states that at Abu Hanifa, if someone says 'they are bad coins' after acknowledging a debt, it is considered a substitution (تبديل) and is invalid even if stated connectedly, whereas at Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), it is considered a valid clarification (بيان) if stated in the same breath. The hashya explains the reasoning: In a commutative contract, the default is that the property is defect-free. Claiming a defect (زيافة) is a retraction (رجوع) of that implied warranty, and retractions are not given effect whether connected or disconnected. This is analogous to claiming a term in a debt or an option in a sale. The second hashya addresses the case where someone acknowledges a debt for the price of a slave-girl and later says 'I did not receive her.' According to Abu Hanifa, this is also a retraction because acknowledging the necessity of the price implies receipt (since the price is due only after receipt in a sale). Therefore, the statement 'I did not receive her' is an invalid retraction. The passage thus distinguishes between a clarification that does not contradict the apparent meaning (accepted at Sahibayn) and a retraction that contradicts the contract's implications (rejected at Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms
التبديل (al-tabdīl): Substitution or change that contradicts the implied terms of a contract, treated as invalid retraction.
البيان (al-bayān): Clarification that explains an ambiguous term without contradicting the contract's implications.
موصول (mawṣūl): A statement that is connected (in the same utterance) to the original acknowledgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The statement is valid only if the coins are actually bad.
D) The statement is a clarification and accepted by all.

Key Takeaway
A statement that contradicts the implied defect-free condition of a commutative contract is always an invalid retraction in the Hanafi school, regardless of being connected.

Classification of Khabar: Mutawatir, Mashhur, Ahad
Defining three categories of hadith transmission with examples and epistemological status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad based on their transmission characteristics and justify the Hanafi conditions for each category.

Core Idea
Khabar is classified into three levels of certainty based on narrator count and continuity: certain (mutawatir), tranquil (mashhur), probable (ahad).

Why are some hadiths absolutely certain while others require scrutiny? This chapter answers that by classifying reports into three types based on their transmission chains. Understanding these categories is essential for evaluating the strength of evidence in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the definitions of mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad. Note the key Arabic terms and their conditions.
The text divides khabar based on multiplicity (kathra) and paucity (qilla) in transmission.
2
Analyze the conditions for mutawatir
The author states two conditions: impossibility of collusion on falsehood due to large numbers, and continuous transmission from beginning to end. Compare with other scholars who add conditions like diversity of location.
Hanafi follows the majority: only two conditions are necessary.
3
Distinguish mashhur from ahad
Mashhur starts as ahad but gains fame in the second and third generations and is accepted by the ummah. This gives it a higher epistemological status than ordinary ahad.
Fame after the third generation does not elevate a report to mashhur.
4
Map epistemological outcomes
Mutawatir yields definitive knowledge (rejection = kufr). Mashhur yields tranquility (rejection = bid'ah). Ahad yields probability (requires further verification).
The practical consequence is how rejecters are treated.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بما قال فيما بعد وفيه نظر؛ لأنّ المتكفّل ببيان الاتصال إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أهل الحديث لا أهل الأصول فكيف انتهض اليه المصنف، فأجيب: بأنّ المراد بيان كيفية الاتصال بأنه بطريق التواتر وغيره وعن حال الرواة أو غيرها فلا مشاحة في هذا فتدبر، كذا في "شرح".١٢
(۱) قوله: [في باب الخبر ... إلخ جواب سؤال مقدّر : وهو أنه إذا كان خبر رسول الله صلّى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلم بمنزلة الكتاب ينبغي أن يكون كلّ خبره عليه السلام متواتراً قطعياً كالكتاب فكيف صار الخبر على ثلاثة أقسام، كذا قيل. ١٢

—( 3 · 4 )·
Chapter on the divisions of khabar. i.e. due to difference in its being established from him. In the chapter of khabar regarding its being established from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and its connection to him, and therefore any khabar. in terms of multiplicity and paucity in transmission. the meaning: khabar became three divisions: a division that is authentic from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and established from him without doubt, and it is mutawatir; and a division in which there is a type of doubt, and it is mashhur; and a division in which there is probability and doubt, and it is ahad. So mutawatir is what a group narrates from a group, such that it is unimaginable that they could agree upon falsehood due to their number, and it reaches you in this manner. Its example: the transmission of the Qur'an, the five obligatory prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, and the amounts of zakat. And mashhur is what starts as ahad then becomes famous in the second and third generations and the ummah receives it with acceptance such that it becomes like mutawatir until it reaches you, and that is mashhur in the second and third generations. Like the hadith of wiping over khuff and stoning in the chapter of zina. Then mutawatir yields definitive knowledge like seeing, and rejecting it is apostasy and disbelief. Mashhur yields knowledge of tranquility, and rejecting it is a violation of Shari'ah and an innovation, and there is no disagreement among scholars regarding the necessity of acting upon both. Rather, the discussion is about ahad. So we say: khabar al-wahid is what is transmitted by one from one, or one from a group, or a group from one, with a number less than tawatur in the advanced eras.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a classification of reports (khabar) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It opens by explaining why khabar is divided into three types: to address the question of why all reports from the Prophet are not mutawatir. The author then defines each type: mutawatir (mass-transmitted, yielding certainty), mashhur (well-known, starting as ahad but gaining acceptance in the second and third generations, yielding tranquility), and ahad (single/isolated reports, containing probability). The commentary elaborates on the conditions for mutawatir, noting that only two conditions are necessary (impossibility of collusion and continuous transmission) while others like diversity of location are debated. It gives examples: mutawatir includes the Quran and essential practices; mashhur includes hadith on wiping over khuff; ahad covers all other reports. The epistemological consequence is highlighted: rejecting mutawatir is kufr, rejecting mashhur is bid'ah, while ahad require further scrutiny. The passage conforms to the Hanafi position that the two conditions for mutawatir are sufficient, following the majority of scholars.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawatir): Narrated by a group from a group such that collusion on falsehood is impossible; yields certainty.
مشهور (mashhur): Starts as ahad but becomes famous in the second and third generations and is accepted by the ummah, giving knowledge of tranquility.
آحاد (ahad): Transmitted by one from one, or one from a group, or a group from one, with less than tawatur count; yields probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of khabar, if rejected, is considered disbelief (kufr)?
A) Khabar mutawatir
B) Khabar mashhur
C) Khabar ahad
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Khabar is classified into mutawatir (certain), mashhur (tranquil), and ahad (probable), each with distinct epistemological weight and consequences for rejection.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Khabar al-Wahid: Definition, Conditions, and Priority over Qiyas
Defining khabar wahid and arguing its precedence over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar al-wahid, list its five conditions for acceptance, and explain why Hanafi usul prioritizes it over qiyas.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid obligates action, not certainty; its priority over qiyas is proven by Companion practice and the foundational certainty of Prophetic speech.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of khabar al-wahid (single-narrator report) and the conditions that make it binding. The passage then moves to a critical argument: why even a weak (in transmission) hadith takes precedence over analogical reasoning (qiyas). Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct istinbat in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define khabar al-wahid and state its hukm
Identify the definition from the opening line and the ruling that it obligates action but not knowledge (yaqin).
The hukm is 'yujibu al-'amal' (obligates action) – not certainty.
2
List the five conditions for acceptance
Extract the conditions: Islam of the narrator, 'adalah, dabt, 'aql, and ittisal al-sanad (connected chain).
Also note that reports from children, disbelievers, or the grossly negligent are not binding.
3
Understand the classification of narrators
The passage divides narrators into those known for ijtihad (e.g., the four caliphs) and famous scribes of revelation (e.g., Ubayy).
Even non-mujtahid narrators can give priority to khabar over qiyas.
4
Analyze the argument for priority over qiyas
The text argues that qiyas has doubt in its foundation (the 'illah is uncertain), while khabar has certainty in its origin (Prophetic speech). Hence, khabar is stronger.
The Companions' practice of abandoning their opinions for hadith is cited as proof.
5
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf with concrete examples
Examples like the hadith of the Bedouin on loud laughter show the practical consequence: Hanafi ruling differs from what qiyas alone would yield.
This also refutes the accusation that Abu Hanifah abandons hadith.

Source Text

فصل في أقسام الخبر أي خبر الواحد. عن واحد ولا عبرة للعدد إذا لم تبلغ حدّ المشهور وهو يوجب العمل به في الأحكام الشرعية بشرط إسلام الراوي وعدالته وضبطه وعقله واتصاله بالخبر. [تعليق: ولا عبرة للعدد] أي لا اعتبار لكثرة العدد إذا كان دون كثرة عدد المشهور، يعني: لا يخرج بهذه الكثرة عن كونه خبراً واحداً. [تعليق: وهو يوجب العمل به] أي: حكم خبر الواحد أنه يوجب العمل ولا يوجب العلم لا علم اليقين ولا علم الطمانينة، وهذا مذهب أكثر أهل العلم وجملة الفقهاء، وذهب أحمد وأكثر المحدثين إلى أنه يوجب علم اليقين، وهذا خلاف ما نجد في أنفسنا من أخبار الآحاد، ووجوب العمل إنما يثبت بشرط إسلام الراوي وعدالته وضبطه وعقله، وغيرها فلا يجب العمل بخبر الكافر والفاسق، وكذا لا يجب العمل بخبر الصبي والمعتوه لفقدان الشروط ولا يجب العمل بخبر الذي اشتدت غفلته بأن كان سهوه ونسيانه أغلب من حفظه. [تعليق: وضبطه] أي: سماع الكلام حق سماعه والفهم بمعناه الذي أريد به ثمّ حفظه ببذل الجد، ثمّ الثبات عليه بمحافظة حدوده ومراقبته بمذاكرته على إساءة الظنّ بنفسه إلى حين أداءه. ثم الراوي في الأصل قسمان: معروف بالعلم والاجتهاد كالخلفاء الأربعة وعبد الله بن مسعود وعبدالله بن عباس وعبدالله بن عمر وزيد بن ثابت ومعاذ بن جبل وأمثالهم، وصحابي مشهور كتب الوحي كأبي بن كعب، وأمثالهم. فإذا صحت عندك روايتهم عن رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام يكون العمل بروايتهم أولى من العمل بالقياس، ولهذا روى محمد رحمه الله حديث الأعرابي في مسئلة القهقهة وترك القياس به، وروى حديث تأخير النساء في مسئلة المحاذاة وترك القياس به، وروى عن عائشة حديث القيء وترك القياس به، وروى عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه حكماً حكم فيه برأيه بحديث سمعه من بلال رضي الله عنه وترك عمر رضي الله عنه رأيه في الجنين وفي دية الأصابع بالحديث وترك ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما رأيه في المزارعة بالحديث الذي سمعه من رافع بن خديج، وأمثاله كثيرة؛ ولأنّ الشبهة في القياس في أصله؛ لأنّ الوصف الذي يلحق بوجوده في الفرع (هو المقيس) بالأصل و (هو المقيس عليه) لا يعلم يقيناً أنّ حكم المقيس عليه معلول به أم لا، والتيقن في الخبر هو الأصل، لأنه كلام الرسول صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلّم وإنّما الشبهة في طريقه بعارض فكان الخبر أقوى من القياس. وليت شعري أن بعض المتعصبين والسفهاء كيف يطعنون على إمامنا الأعظم وهمامنا الأقدم وهو يقدم الخبر الضعيف على القياس فالحذر الحذر من قولهم. [تعليق: حديث الأعرابي] وهو ما روي أنّ النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلّي وأصحابه خلفه، فجاء أعرابي فوقع في بئر فضحك بعض أصحابه فلما فرغ عن الصلاة، قال: «من ضحك منكم قهقهةً فليعد الوضوء والصلاة جميعاً»، والقياس فيه أن لا يكون ناقضاً؛ لأنّ علّة نقض الطهارة هي خروج النجاسة؛ لأنّ اتصاف البدن بالنجاسة مما ينافي اتصافه بالطهارة وفي القهقهة ليس ذلك أي: فترك القياس بهذا الحديث وإن قلت راوي الحديث سعيد الجهني وهو لم يعرف بالفقه والاجتهاد بين الصحابة فكيف يصلح هذا مثالاً أو تفريعاً أو تائيداً، قلت: قد رواه أبو موسى الأشعري أيضاً وهو معروف الفقه بينهم. [تعليق: حديث القيء] وهو ما روي أنه قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من قاء أو رعف في صلاة فلينصرف وليتوضأ وليبن صلاته ما لم يتكلّم»، والقياس يقتضي أن لا يفسد الوضوء بالرعاف والقيء؛ لأنّ الخارج ليس بنجس؛ لأنه خرج من أعلى المعدة وهو ليس بمحلّ النجاسة، فإن قلت: المرّة والبلغم والطعام المختلفة بها رطوبات نجسة ولذا يتنفّر عنها الطبع قلت لو كان هذه الأشياء نجسة لاستوي فيها القليل والكثير كما في دم السائل، وروي هذا الحديث عن عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها وهي فقيهة الأمّة، قال عليه السلام في شأنها: «خذوا من هذه الحميراء ثلثي دينكم».
Chapter on the divisions of khabar, meaning khabar al-wahid. From one person, and there is no consideration for number if it does not reach the limit of mashhur. It obligates acting upon it in shar'i rulings on condition of the narrator's Islam, integrity ('adalah), precision (dabt), intellect, and connection to the khabar. [Commentary on 'there is no consideration for number'] means there is no consideration for multiplicity of number if it is less than the multiplicity of mashhur, i.e., this multiplicity does not remove it from being khabar wahid. [Commentary on 'it obligates acting upon it'] means the ruling of khabar wahid is that it obligates action and does not obligate knowledge—neither knowledge of certainty nor knowledge of tranquility. This is the madhhab of most people of knowledge and the majority of jurists. Ahmad and most muhaddithin held that it obligates knowledge of certainty, and this contradicts what we find in ourselves regarding ahad reports. The obligation of action is only established with the condition of the narrator's Islam, integrity, precision, intellect, etc. So the report of a disbeliever or sinner does not obligate action, nor that of a child or insane person due to lack of conditions, nor that of one whose forgetfulness predominates. [Commentary on 'his precision'] means hearing the speech properly, understanding its intended meaning, then memorizing it with effort, then sticking to it by guarding its limits and reviewing it while thinking ill of oneself until the time of narration. Then the narrator in principle is of two types: one known for knowledge and ijtihad like the four caliphs, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abdullah ibn Umar, Zayd ibn Thabit, Mu'adh ibn Jabal and their like; and a famous companion who wrote the revelation like Ubayy ibn Ka'b and their like. So when you are certain of their narration from the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him), acting upon their narration is more worthy than acting upon qiyas. For this reason, Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated the hadith of the Bedouin concerning the issue of loud laughter and abandoned qiyas for it; and he narrated the hadith of delaying women concerning the issue of alignment and abandoned qiyas for it; and he narrated from Aisha the hadith of vomiting and abandoned qiyas for it; and he narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) a ruling in which he had given his opinion based on a hadith he heard from Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him); and Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) abandoned his opinion regarding the fetus and regarding the blood-money of fingers for a hadith; and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) abandoned his opinion regarding sharecropping for the hadith he heard from Rafi' ibn Khadij; and there are many similar examples. And because the doubt in qiyas is in its foundation, because the attribute that attaches to the branch (the analogized) from the original (that which is analogized upon) is not known with certainty whether the ruling of the original is caused by it or not. Contrary to that, certainty in the khabar is the original, because it is the speech of the Messenger (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), and the doubt is only in its chain as an external factor. Thus, khabar is stronger than qiyas. I wonder how some fanatics and foolish people attack our great Imam and our ancient leader when he prefers a weak hadith over qiyas. So beware, beware of their words. [Commentary on the hadith of the Bedouin] It is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was praying with his companions behind him. A Bedouin came and fell into a well, and some companions laughed. When he finished the prayer, he said: 'Whoever laughed loudly, let him repeat the wudu and the prayer together.' Qiyas in this matter would dictate that it is not nullifying, because the cause of nullifying purification is the exit of impurity; the body's being described with impurity contradicts its being described with purity, and in loud laughter that is not present. So he abandoned qiyas due to this hadith. Even if you say the narrator of the hadith is Sa'id al-Juhani, who is not known for fiqh and ijtihad among the companions, how can this be an example or a branch or a support? I say: Abu Musa al-Ash'ari also narrated it, and he is known for fiqh among them. [Commentary on the hadith of vomiting] It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever vomits or has a nosebleed in prayer, let him leave and perform wudu and then resume his prayer as long as he has not spoken.' Qiyas would require that wudu is not invalidated by nosebleed and vomiting, because the exiting matter is not impure, since it comes from the upper stomach which is not a place of impurity. If you say: gall, phlegm, and food that has changed are impure moistures, and the natural disposition is repulsed by them, I say: if these things were impure, the small and large amounts would be the same, as with flowing blood. This hadith was narrated by Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), who was the jurist of the nation. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding her: 'Take from this Humayra' two-thirds of your religion.'
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a definition and elaboration of khabar al-wahid (single-narrator hadith) within Hanafi usul. It opens by stating that khabar al-wahid is a report from one narrator (or a number below mashhur) and that it obligates action (yujibu al-'amal) but not certainty (yaqin). The author emphasizes the conditions for accepting such a report: the narrator must be Muslim, just ('adil), precise (dabit), rational, and the chain must be connected. The commentary further clarifies that number alone does not elevate it to mashhur status, and that the obligation to act is conditional on these qualities; reports from disbelievers, sinners, children, or the mentally deficient are not binding. The precision (dabt) is defined as proper hearing, understanding, memorization, and careful preservation up to the time of narration. Next, the text classifies narrators into two categories: those renowned for knowledge and ijtihad (like the four caliphs and prominent companions) and famous companions associated with writing revelation (like Ubayy ibn Ka'b). The central argument then becomes: when a narration from such trustworthy narrators is authenticated, acting upon it takes precedence over qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author provides evidence from the practice of the Companions, citing examples where famous figures like Umar and Ibn Umar abandoned their own opinions for a hadith. Specific examples are given: the hadith of the Bedouin regarding loud laughter in prayer (which causes both wudu and prayer to be repeated), the hadith of delaying women in congregational alignment, the hadith of vomiting, and others. The rationale is that qiyas is inherently doubtful because the cause ('illah) linking the original and branch is not certain, whereas a hadith from the Prophet is certain in origin, with doubt only in transmission. Therefore, even a weak hadith (in the sense of lesser strength) is preferred over qiyas. The author defends Imam Abu Hanifah against critics who accuse him of disregarding hadith, clarifying that the Imam actually prioritizes hadith over qiyas.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): خبر يرويه واحد أو عدد دون حد المشهور، يوجب العمل ولا يوجب العلم
العدالة (al-'adalah): كون الراوي مسلما غير فاسق، وهو شرط لقبول خبر الواحد
الضبط (al-dabt): سماع الكلام حق سماعه، وفهم معناه المراد، وحفظه بجد، وثباته عليه حتى يؤدي
القياس (al-qiyas): إلحاق فرع بأصل في حكم بعلة جامعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the hukm (ruling) of khabar al-wahid?
A) It obligates action and produces certain knowledge (yaqin).
B) It obligates action but does not produce certainty.
C) It is to be rejected unless it reaches the level of tawatur.
D) It is accepted only if narrated by a mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
Khabar al-wahid obligates action, not certainty, and takes precedence over qiyas because its origin is certain while qiyas is inherently doubtful.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Principle of General Need (عموم بلوى) in Hanafi Usul
States the usul principle that lack of widespread transmission for a matter of general need indicates unsoundness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of عموم بلوى to evaluate whether a solitary hadith is acceptable in the Hanafi school and distinguish between cases where a single report is accepted (informing) versus rejected (testimony).

Core Idea
If a ruling is needed by everyone, its evidence must be widely known: a solitary report in matters of general need indicates unsoundness.

This lesson introduces a cornerstone of Hanafi hadith criticism: the principle of عموم بلوى. Instead of relying solely on chain analysis, Hanafi scholars consider whether a hadith addresses a matter so universally needed that it would have been widely transmitted. This principle explains why certain well-known hadiths in other schools—like reciting the Basmalah aloud or raising hands in prayer—are not acted upon by Hanafis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter
Determine if the hadith concerns a matter of general need that affects all or most Muslims frequently, such that it would be needed daily or regularly.
The test is: does every mukallaf need to know this ruling?
2
Check transmission level
Ask: Has this hadith reached the level of istifadha or tawatur? If it is only a khabar wahid (solitary report), apply the presumption of عموم بلوى.
For a matter of general need, a solitary transmission is a red flag.
3
Apply the principle
Conclude that the lack of widespread transmission despite عموم بلوى is a sign of unsoundness (abrogation or invalidity). The hadith is not acted upon in the Hanafi school.
This is not a rejection by opinion but by a usul maxim.
4
Distinguish ikhbar from shahada
In matters of informing (ikhbar), a single trustworthy report may be accepted. In formal testimony (shahada), the standard of two witnesses is required.
Example: breastfeeding after marriage (radā' ṭāri') is ikhbar; the marriage contract validity is shahada.
5
Apply to examples
Work through the examples in the text: audible basmalah, raising hands, touching penis, water impurity, qibla direction. Note which accept a single report and why.
The principle explains many Hanafi positions on furū'.

Source Text

فصل في أقسام الخبر
والثاني؛ لأنهم لا يتهمون بالتقصير في متابعة السنة فإذا لم يشتهر الخبر مع شدة الحاجة وعموم البلوى كان ذلك علامة عدم صحته، ومثاله في الحكميات إذا أخبر واحد أنّ امرأته حرمت عليه بالرضاع الطاري جاز أن يعتمد على خبره ويتزوج أختها ولو أخبر أنّ العقد كان باطلاً بحكم الرضاع لا يقبل خبره، وكذلك إذا أخبرت المرأة بموت زوجها أو طلاقه إياها وهو غائب جاز أن تعتمد على خبره وتتزوج بغيره، ولو اشتبهت عليه القبلة فأخبره واحد عنها وجب العمل به ولو وجد ماء لا يعلم حاله فأخبره واحد عن النجاسة لا يتوضأ به بل يتيمم.
وهو ما روى أبو هريرة رضي الله تعالى عنه: «كان النبي صلّى الله تعالى عليه وسلّم جهر بـ«بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم في «الصلاة فإنّ أمر التسمية مما يعم به البلوى؛ لأنّ هذه حادثة تكرّر في كل يوم و ليلة بالنسبة إلى جميع المكلفين، فلو كان هذا الخبر معمولاً لاشتهر فيما بينهم، كذا في "الفصول".
(۱) قوله : [ كان ذلك ... إلخ ] أي علامة عدم شهرته فيما بينهم فيما يعم به البلوى أمارة على نسخه أو بطلانه وهو مذهب أبي الحسن الكرخي من أصحابنا وهو مختار المتأخرين، ولذا لا نعمل بخبر الجهر بالتسمية وخبر رفع اليدين عند الركوع والرفع منه وخبر مس الذكر وخبر الوضوء ممّا مسته النار وغيرها حيث يحتاج فيه إلى كمال الشيوع والإستفاضة؛ لأنه مما يعم به البلوى وهي مما يحتاج إلى معرفتها الخاصة والعامة وقد بقيت على الأحاد و لم يصل إلى حدّ التلقي، وهذا وجه آخر لترجيح أخبارنا على أخبارهم في هذه الأبواب وليس هذا ردّ الخبر بالرأي والقياس، بل هو ترجيح ما تتشبث به من الأحاديث وعند عامة الأصوليين يقبل إذا صح سنده فافهم، كذا في "المعدن".
(۲) قوله: بالرضاع الطاري] أي: على النكاح بأن تزوج رجل صغيرةً، فأخبر ثقة أنها قد ارتضعت من أمة لها أو أخته يجوز الاعتماد على خبره، فتحرم الصغيرة على الزوج؛ لأنها صارت أخته رضاعاً.
(۳) قوله: [لا يقبل خبره] فلا يحكم ببطلان العقد وتفريقهما بمجرد خبرها أنها أرضعتهما، فلا يتزوّج بأختها؛ لأنّ خبرها مخالف للظاهر؛ لأنّ النكاح حصل بشهرة وحضور جماعة، فلو كان الرضاع ثابتاً لم يخف عليهما وعلى الشهود وأقربائهما أنّ بينهما سبب حرمة، ومن حيث إنه لم يشتهر دلّ أنه غير بخلاف الرضاع الطاري؛ لأنه لا يخالف الظاهر، ثُمّ هذا كله فتوى وقضاء، وأما التقوى والديانة فهو أن يدعها لهذه الشبهة، وقد أخرج الترمذي في سننه عن عقبة ابن الحارث أنه تزوج امرأة، فجاءت امرأة سوداء، وقالت: إني أرضعتكما قال: فأتيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلّم، فقلتُ: تزوّجتُ فلانة بنت فلان فجاءتنا امرأة سوداء، فقالت : إنّي أرضعتكما وهي كاذبة، قال: فأعرض عني، قال: فأتيته من قبل وجهه، فقلتُ: إنّها كاذبة، قال: وكيف بها وقد زعمت أنها قد أرضعتكما دعها عنك، قال : وهذا حديث حسن صحيح والعمل على هذا عند بعض أهل العلم من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلّم ومن بعدهم أجازوا شهادة المرأة الواحدة في الرضاع، وبه يقول أحمد وإسحق، وقال بعض أهل العلم لا يجوز شهادة امرأة واحدة في الرضاع وهو قول الشافعي عليه الرحمة، فالجمهور على أنه لا يثبت إلا بنصاب الشهادة فافهم، كذا في "الحصول".
(۱) قوله: [جاز أن تعتمد على خبره لعدم مخالفة الظاهر؛ لأنه ليس ثَمّه دليل مكذب لخبر الواحد فيقبل خبره ووجب العمل به، ثُمّ اعلم أنّ هذا في الإخبار، وأما في الشهادة فلا يصح وإن كان الشاهد اثنين حيث لا يقضي القاضي بالفرقة؛ لأنه قضاء على الغائب، كذا في "النهاية".
Section on Types of Reports. The second [type]; because they are not accused of negligence in following the Sunnah, so if the report is not widespread despite severe need and general applicability, that is a sign of its unsoundness. Its example in legal matters: if a single person reports that his wife has been made forbidden to him by subsequent breastfeeding, it is permissible to rely on his report and marry her sister; but if she reports that the contract was invalid due to breastfeeding, her report is not accepted. Similarly, if a woman reports her husband's death or divorce while he is absent, she may rely on his report and marry another. If the direction of the qibla is uncertain and a single person informs him of it, he must act on it. If he finds water whose state is unknown and a single person informs him of its impurity, he should not perform ablution with it but should perform tayammum. This is what Abu Huraira narrated: 'The Prophet used to recite “Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim” aloud in prayer,' for the matter of the Basmalah is of general need, as this incident recurs every day and night for all legally responsible persons. Had this report been acted upon, it would have become widespread among them, as in “al-Fusul”. (1) His words: [That would be... etc.] i.e., that a lack of its prevalence among them in a matter of general need is a sign of its abrogation or invalidity. This is the doctrine of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi among our scholars, and it is the choice of the later scholars. Hence we do not act upon the report of audible Basmalah, the report of raising hands at bowing and rising, the report of touching the penis, the report of ablution from things touched by fire, and others, where complete widespread transmission is needed; because it is a matter of general need that requires knowledge by both the elite and the common people, yet these reports remained as solitary narrations and did not reach the level of acceptance. This is another way to prefer our reports over theirs in these chapters, and this is not rejection of reports by opinion and analogy, but rather a preference for what we adhere to from the hadiths. According to general usuli scholars, it is accepted if its chain is sound, so understand. As in “al-Ma'dan”. (2) His words: [by subsequent breastfeeding] i.e., upon the marriage: for example, a man marries a young girl, and a trustworthy person reports that she has been breastfed by his slave woman or sister – it is permissible to rely on his report, so the young girl becomes forbidden to the husband because she becomes his sister by breastfeeding. (3) His words: [His report is not accepted] So the invalidity of the contract and their separation is not judged merely by her report that she breastfed them both, so he does not marry her sister because her report contradicts the apparent; for the marriage occurred publicly with the presence of a group. Had the breastfeeding been established, it would not have been hidden from them, the witnesses, and their relatives that between them there was a cause of prohibition. The fact that it was not widespread indicates that it is otherwise, unlike the subsequent breastfeeding because it does not contradict the apparent. Then all this is for legal opinion and judgment; as for piety and religious observance, he should leave her due to this doubt. At-Tirmidhi narrated in his Sunan from 'Uqbah ibn al-Harith that he married a woman, then a black woman came and said, 'I breastfed both of you.' He said, 'I came to the Prophet and said, I married so-and-so daughter of so-and-so, and a black woman came to us and said, I breastfed both of you, and she is lying.' He said, 'He turned away from me.' He said, 'I came to him from the front and said, She is lying.' He said, 'How can it be when she claimed she breastfed both of you? Leave her.' He said, 'This is a hasan sahih hadith, and it is acted upon by some scholars among the Companions and those after them, who permitted the testimony of one woman in breastfeeding. Ahmad and Ishaq hold this view. Some scholars said it is not permissible to have the testimony of one woman in breastfeeding, which is the view of al-Shafi'i. The majority hold that it is only established by the required number of witnesses, so understand. As in “al-Husul”. (1) His words: [It is permissible to rely on his report] because it does not contradict the apparent; there is no evidence to falsify the solitary report, so his report is accepted and must be acted upon. Then know that this is for informing; as for testimony, it is not valid even if there are two witnesses, where the judge does not rule for separation because it would be a judgment against an absent person. As in “al-Nihayah”.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi with its commentary (Hashiya) presents a fundamental principle of the Hanafi usul: A hadith that pertains to a matter of general need (عموم بلوى) must be widely transmitted to be accepted. If it remains a solitary report (khabar wahid) despite the general need, that is a sign of its unsoundness, either because it is abrogated or because it is not authentic. This principle is attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and is the relied-upon position of the later Hanafi scholars. The passage gives several examples: the hadiths about reciting 'Bismillah' aloud, raising the hands in prayer, touching the penis breaking wudu, and performing wudu after eating food touched by fire—all are rejected because they concern matters that occur frequently for all Muslims, so they should have been widely known. The commentary also discusses the distinction between reports that contradict the apparent (like a wife claiming the marriage contract was invalid due to prior breastfeeding) and those that do not (like a subsequent breastfeeding). In the first case, the report is not accepted because the original contract was public and widely witnessed. In the second, the report is accepted because it does not contradict any established fact. The passage also covers other scenarios: a woman trusting a report of her husband's death or divorce, relying on a single person for the qibla direction, and the case of water whose purity is uncertain—if a single person reports it is impure, one should not use it but perform tayammum. Finally, the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn al-Harith is cited, showing that the Prophet accepted a single woman's claim of breastfeeding, leading to a madhhab dispute: Ahmad and Ishaq accept one woman's testimony in breastfeeding, while al-Shafi'i requires the normal number of witnesses. The Hanafi position, as indicated in the commentary, is that in matters of informing (ikhbar), a single report may be accepted, but in testimony (shahada), the standard is stricter.

Key Terms
عموم بلوى (umum balwa): A matter of general need that affects all or most legally responsible individuals frequently, such that if a hadith existed regarding it, it would necessarily become widely known.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A report transmitted by a single narrator (or a small number) that does not reach the level of tawatur or istifada.
رضاع طاري (rada' tari): Breastfeeding that occurs after the marriage contract, which does not contradict the apparent validity of the marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are hadiths like the audible basmalah and raising hands in prayer not accepted in the Hanafi school?
A) Because their chains are weak or contain unknown narrators.
B) Because they contradict the Quranic injunction on prayer.
C) Because they pertain to a matter of general need (عموم بلوى) yet were not widely transmitted, indicating they are abrogated or invalid.
D) Because Abu Hanifa ruled against them based on his own reasoning without textual basis.

Key Takeaway
The principle of عموم بلوى is a Hanafi tool for evaluating hadith: if a matter is universally needed and the hadith remains solitary, its unsoundness is presumed.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Precedence of Text over Opinion and the Two Types of Shubha
States the usul rule that textual evidence prevails over opinion and distinguishes two types of legal doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why textual evidence (khabar) takes precedence over personal opinion (ra'y) and distinguish between shubha fi al-mahall and shubha fi al-zann, applying the Hanafi principle to examples of hadd punishment.

Core Idea
Textual evidence overrides opinion; shubha fi al-mahall (text-based doubt) is stronger than shubha fi al-zann (opinion-based doubt).

This foundational usul passage from Al-Shashi establishes a key hierarchy in Hanafi legal methodology: when explicit textual evidence (khabar) is available, it must be followed over personal reasoning or opinion (ra'y). It then introduces a crucial distinction between two types of legal doubt (shubha) that affect the application of hadd punishments. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rule that textual doubt overrides personal belief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Find the statement in the passage that establishes the precedence of text over opinion. Note the examples given (qibla direction, pure water) to see the rule in action.
The rule is stated early: لا سبيل إلى العمل بالرأي مع إمكان العمل بالنص.
2
Understand the two types of shubha
The passage introduces shubha fi al-mahall (doubt in the subject, based on a textual proof) and shubha fi al-zann (doubt in opinion, based on personal conjecture). Distinguish their sources and relative strength.
Shubha fi al-mahall is stronger because it originates from a shar'i dalil.
3
Analyze the father-son examples
Work through the two cases: father with son's slave-girl (shubha fi al-mahall applies, no hadd) and son with father's slave-girl (shubha fi al-zann applies, hadd depends on belief). Identify which type of shubha operates in each.
The hadith 'أنت ومالك لأبيك' creates the textual doubt for the father.
4
Derive the usul principle
Using the hadith as a proof, apply the Hanafi usul rule that general texts (amm) indicate permissibility or obligation. Show how this leads to the ruling that the father's doubt is text-based and overrides his personal opinion.
This step connects the fiqh example to usul al-fiqh.
5
Evaluate the epistemological weight
Recognize why shubha fi al-mahall is stronger: it does not depend on the individual's belief, whereas shubha fi al-zann does. This affects the outcome of rulings like hadd and lineage.
The hashya stresses that shubha fi al-mahall exists even if the perpetrator believes it is forbidden.

فصل الواجب على المجتهد لأنه أقوى من الرأي. ١٢ مرّ ذكره، فإنّه لا سبيل إلى العمل بالرأي مع إمكان العمل بالنص، ولهذا إذا أي عدم جواز العمل بالراي مع أي القبلة. ١٢ أي من اشتبهت عليه القبلة. ١٢ إمكان العمل بالأقوى منه. ١٢ اشتبهت عليه القبلة فأخبره واحد عنها لا يجوز له التحري ولو وجد ماء أي من وجد. ١٢ أي الماء. ١٢ أي الماء النجس. ٢ لـ فأخبره عدل أنه نجس لا يجوز له التوضي به بل يتيمم، وعلي اعتبار أن العمل لأن الخبر متقدم على الراي. ١٢ (1) لاستناده إلى الراي والظن. ١٢ بالرأي دون العمل بالنصّ، قلنا: إنّ الشبهة بالمحلّ أقوى من الشبهة في الظنّ وهو الشبهة في المحل. ١٢ حتى سقط اعتبار ظنّ العبد في الفصل الأوّل ومثاله في ما إذا وطى جارية وكذا جارية بنته. ١٢ حد الزنا. ١٢. أي جارية ابنه. ١٢ الأب الواطى. ١٢ أي الواطي. ١٢ ابنه لا يحد وان قال: «علمت أنها علي حرام» " ويثبت نسب الولد منه لأنّ للأب الواطي. ١٢ وصلية. ١٢ أي للأب الواطي. ١٢ شبهة الملك له تثبت بالنصّ في مال الابن قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «أنت ومالك لأبيك فسقط إعتبار ظنه في الحل والحرمة في ذلك ولو وطئ الابن جارية أبيه يعتبر ظنّه في الحل والحرمة حتى لو قال: «ظننت أنها علي حرام» يجب الحد، ولو قال: ظننت أنها علي حلال» لا يجب الحد"؛ لأنّ شبهة الملك في مال الأب لم يثبت له بالنص فاعتبر رأيه ولا يثبت نسب الولد وإن ادعاه. (۱) قوله : [ إن الشبهة بالمحل أقوى ... إلخ] أي: بالفعل وتسمّى شبهة الاشتباه؛ لأنها كانت نشأت من الظنّ، فيكون لها ثلثة أسماء شبهة الاشتباه وشبهة الفعل وشبهة الظنّ، اعلم أن الشبهة ما يشبه الثابت :أي: الحق وليس بثابت وهي قد تكون شبهة بالفعل وتسمى شبهة اشتباه وهي بالشبهة في الظنّ، وذلك أن يظنّ الإنسان ما ليس بدليل الحل والحرمة دليلاً في كل واحد منهما، وقد تكون شبهة في المحل وتسمّى شبهة الدليل والشبهة الحكميّة وهي أن يوجد الدليل الشرعي النافي للحلّ والحرمة مع تخلّف حكمه لمانع اتصل به فيورث هذا الدليل شبهة في حلّ ما ليس بحلال أو عكسه، وهذا النوع من الشبهة لا يتوقف تحققه على ظنّ الجاني واعتقاده بخلاف القسم الأوّل، فإذا تحقق كلاهما أي كلا الشبهتان فلا بد من أن يكون القسم الثاني من الشبهة في المحل لنشوه عن النص أقوى من الأوّل لاستناده إلى الرأي والظنّ، ولهذا كان الحدّ ساقطاً لشبهة المحلّ وإن كان على خلاف ظنّه فتدبّر، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (۲) قوله: [ومثاله] :أي مثال ما كانت الشبهة في المحل و في الظنّ ومثال سقوط ظنّ العبد فيما إذا كانت الشبهة في المحل وعدم سقوط ظنّه فيما إذا كانت الشبهة في الظنّ، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (۳) قوله: [أنها عليّ حرام] أي: إذا قال الرجل: «إنّها علي حرام»، وقالت جارية الابن: «ظننت أنه يحــــل لي لايحدّ واحد منهما، أما المرأة فلدعوى الشبهة وأما الرجل فلان الزنا يقوم بهما فإذا سقط الحد عن المرأة سقط عن الرجل مكان الشركة. القوله: [ولا يثبت نسب الولد... إلخ] لأنّ الفعل تمحض زنا في نفسه، لكن بحكم الاشتباه يسقط الحدّ وهذا الاشتباه لا يوجب ثبوت النسب؛ لأنّ ثبوته يعتمد قيام الملك في المحلّ من وجه أو قيام المحلّ فيـــه ولم يوجد بخلاف الشبهة في المحل؛ لأنها نشأت عن دليل شرعي وهو قوله عليه السلام: «أنت ومالك لأبيك» وهو قائم فلا يفرق الحال بين الظنّ وعدمه في سقوط الحد. ١٢
Chapter: The Obligation on the Mujtahid. Because it is stronger than opinion. It was mentioned earlier; indeed, there is no way to act on opinion when acting on the text is possible. Hence, if someone is uncertain about the qibla, and one person informs him of it, he may not engage in ijtihad (taharrī). And if he finds water, and a trustworthy person informs him that it is impure, he may not perform ablution with it but must perform tayammum. It is based on the principle that the report (khabar) takes precedence over opinion. [Footnote 1: Because it relies on opinion and conjecture.] But we say: the doubt in the subject (shubha fi al-mahall) is stronger than the doubt in the opinion (shubha fi al-zann). Thus the consideration of a person's opinion is dropped in the first case. Its example: if a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl or his daughter's slave-girl, he is not subject to the hadd punishment even if he says 'I knew it was forbidden for me', and the lineage of the child is established from him, because the father has the legal doubt of ownership established by textual proof in his son's property – the Prophet ﷺ said: 'You and your property belong to your father.' So his opinion regarding permissibility and prohibition is disregarded. And if a son has intercourse with his father's slave-girl, his opinion is considered regarding permissibility and prohibition; so if he says 'I thought it was forbidden for me', the hadd is obligatory, and if he says 'I thought it was permissible for me', the hadd is not obligatory, because the doubt of ownership in the father's property is not established for him by text, so his opinion is considered. And the lineage of the child is not established even if he claims it. [Then the hashya expands on the definitions and examples.]
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes a key usul rule: when textual evidence (khabar) is available, it takes precedence over opinion (ra'y), which includes ijtihad or personal reasoning. The text uses practical examples: if a person is uncertain of the qibla direction and a single reliable person tells him the direction, he must follow that report and cannot resort to his own ijtihad (taharrī). Similarly, if he finds water but a trustworthy person informs him it is najis, he cannot use it for wudu but must do tayammum. The underlying principle is that khabar (report) is stronger than opinion. The text then introduces a distinction between two types of doubt (shubha): shubha fi al-mahall (doubt in the subject, arising from a textual proof) and shubha fi al-zann (doubt in opinion, based on personal conjecture). Shubha fi al-mahall is stronger because it originates from a textual source. This is illustrated with examples from hadd punishments for zina. A father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl is not punished, because the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father' creates a textual doubt of ownership (shubha fi al-mahall), even if the father thought it was forbidden. Conversely, a son who has intercourse with his father's slave-girl is subject to hadd if he thought it was forbidden, because no such textual doubt exists for him; his opinion is considered. The hashya further clarifies that shubha fi al-mahall does not depend on the perpetrator's belief, while shubha fi al-zann does. The passage ends with the note that lineage is only established when there is a textual doubt of ownership, not when the doubt is merely based on opinion.

Key Terms
الشبهة (al-shubha): A legal doubt that resembles a valid proof but is not actually valid; it can avert punishments.
شبهة في المحل (shubha fi al-mahall): Doubt in the subject, arising from a textual proof (dalil shar'i) that creates a semblance of legality, even if the ruling is absent due to a connected impediment.
شبهة في الظن (shubha fi al-zann): Doubt in opinion, based on personal conjecture or mistaken belief about what is a valid proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl and says he knew it was forbidden?
A) He faces the hadd punishment for zina.
B) He does not face the hadd punishment because of shubha fi al-mahall.
C) He does not face the hadd punishment because he thought it was forbidden.
D) He faces the hadd punishment only if he admitted it was forbidden.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, textual evidence overrides personal opinion, and shubha fi al-mahall (derived from text) carries more weight than shubha fi al-zann (based on conjecture), affecting rulings like hadd and lineage.

Types of Descriptions in Qiyas and Their Strength
Explains three types of descriptions and their analogy to witness testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of descriptions (wasf) in Hanafi qiyas, state their evidentiary strength, and apply the analogy of witness testimony to determine when a description compels action (wujub) versus merely permits it (jawaz).

Core Idea
In Hanafi qiyas, only a description whose causality is proven by text or consensus compels action; mere suitability only permits.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi introduces a foundational classification in Hanafi legal theory: the types of descriptions (al-awṣāf) that can serve as effective causes (ʿilal) in analogical reasoning (qiyās). By comparing these descriptions to different levels of witness testimony, the author clarifies when a qiyās is binding and when it is merely permissible. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly applying qiyās in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Locate in the passage the three types of descriptions: (1) from textual nass, (2) from ijma, (3) from ijtihad. Note the Arabic terms used.
2
Understand their evidentiary strength
Each type has a different strength: the first compels action (yūjib al-ʿamal), the second also compels but with a condition (appearance of effect in a place of ijma), the third only permits (yujawwiz) but does not compel.
The key factor is 'ghalabat al-zann' – predominant opinion that the description is the cause.
3
Apply the witness analogy
Match each type to the corresponding witness status: first type = fully certified witness (after tazkiya), second = witness with apparent justice (before certification), third = witness of unknown character (mastūr).
4
Recognize the condition for binding qiyas
The passage states that for a description to necessitate action, its effect (athar) must have appeared in a place of consensus or text. Otherwise, a suitable difference (al-farq al-munāsib) can invalidate the qiyas.
This shows that mere suitability is not sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القياس الشرعي. إذا رأينا وصفا مناسبا للحكم وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يغلب الظنّ بإضافة الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف وغلبة الظن في الشرع توجب العمل عند انعدام ما فوقها من الدليل. بمنزلة المسافر إذا غلب على ظنّه أن بقربه ماء لم يجز له التيمم. وحكم هذا القياس أن يبطل بالفرق المناسب؛ لأنه يوجد مناسب سواه في صورة الحكم فلا يبقى الظنّ بإضافة الحكم إليه فلا يثبت الحكم به؛ لأنه كان بناء على غلبة الظنّ وقد بطل ذلك بالفرق. وقد ظهر أثر هذا الوصف في موضع الإجماع وهو ولاية المال، فإنّها ثابتة في مال الصغير بالإجماع. وإنّما يشترط هذا لوجوب العمل بالوصف؛ لأنّ الوصف في القياس بمنزلة الشاهد وهو اجتنابه عن محظورات دينه واجتنابه عنها يدلّ ظاهراً على أنه يجتنب عن الكذب في الشهاده أيضاً فظهور أثر لوصف في موضع آخر يدلّ ظاهراً على أنه مؤثر في موضع النزاع فهذا يوجب العمل بالقياس بهذه العلة، وأما مجرّد المناسبة فيجوزه ولا يوجبه. هذا كان العمل بالنوع الأوّل بمنزلة الحكم بالشهادة بعد تزكية الشاهد وتعديله والنوع الثاني بمنزلة الشهادة عند ظهور العدالة قبل التزكية والنوع الثالث بمنزلة شهادة المستور.
Chapter on Legal Analogy. When we see a description suitable for the ruling and the ruling has been associated with it in a place of consensus, the predominant opinion (zann) adds the ruling to that description, and predominant opinion in the Sharia necessitates action in the absence of evidence above it. It is like a traveler who is strongly of the opinion that water is near him – he is not permitted to perform tayammum. The ruling of this analogy is that it is invalidated by a suitable difference because a suitable (description) other than it exists in the case (of the ruling), so the predominant opinion of adding the ruling to it does not remain, thus the ruling is not established by it because it was based on predominant opinion and that has been invalidated by the difference. And the effect of this description has appeared in a place of consensus, which is the guardianship of wealth, for it is established for the property of a minor by consensus. And this condition is required for the obligation of acting upon the description because the description in analogy is like the witness: his avoidance of prohibited acts in his religion indicates apparently that he avoids lying in testimony as well. So the appearance of the effect of a description in another place indicates apparently that it is effective in the disputed place, and this necessitates acting upon analogy with this cause. As for mere suitability, it permits it but does not obligate it. Thus, acting upon the first type is like ruling by testimony after the witness has been qualified and certified. The second type is like testimony when justice appears before certification. The third type is like the testimony of a person of unknown character.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the Hanafi theory of qiyas (analogy) and the conditions under which a description (وصف) can be considered a valid 'illa (cause) for extending a ruling from an original case (أصل) to a new case (فرع). The text distinguishes three types of descriptions based on how they are established: (1) those explicitly stated in the Qur'an or Sunnah (النوع الأول), (2) those deduced from consensus (الإجماع), and (3) those derived through ijtihad and pure reasoning (الرأي والاجتهاد). The author uses the analogy of witness testimony to illustrate their strength: the first type is like a fully qualified witness after formal certification (تزكية), the second type is like a witness whose justice is apparent but not formally certified, and the third type is like a witness of unknown character (مستور). The key principle is that only strong predominant opinion (غلبة الظن) arising from a description that has shown its effect in a place of consensus or text can compel action (يوجب العمل). Mere suitability (مجرد المناسبة) only permits action (يجوزه) but does not obligate it. This aligns with the Hanafi position that qiyas requires a strong link between the description and the ruling, otherwise the analogy can be invalidated by pointing out a suitable difference (الفرق المناسب) that breaks the presumed connection.

Key Terms
القياس الشرعي (al-qiyas al-shar'i): The legal process of extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause (illa).
الوصف المناسب (al-wasf al-munasib): A description that is suitable (appropriate) as a potential cause for a ruling, but not yet proven to be the actual cause.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion or strong conjecture that reaches a high degree of certainty, sufficient to necessitate action in legal matters when no stronger evidence exists.
النوع الأول (al-naw' al-awwal): The description whose causality is explicitly stated in the Quran or Sunnah (النص), giving it the highest evidentiary strength.
النوع الثاني (al-naw' al-thani): The description whose causality is established by consensus (الإجماع), showing its effect in a case agreed upon by all scholars.
النوع الثالث (al-naw' al-thalith): The description derived through ijtihad and reasoning (الرأي والاجتهاد), which is merely suitable and does not compel action by itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of description in qiyas is analogous to the testimony of a witness whose justice is apparent but not formally certified?
A) The first type (description from nass)
B) The second type (description from ijma)
C) The third type (description from ijtihad)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the binding force of a qiyas depends on the strength of the description's causal link: only descriptions from nass or ijma compel action; those from ijtihad permit it but do not obligate.

Type 1 of Qalb: True Inversion (Qalb Haqiqi)
Explaining type 1 qalb with conditions and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for type 1 qalb and apply it to invalidate an opponent's ta'lil by swapping the 'illa and ma'lul.

Core Idea
Type 1 qalb swaps the opponent's 'illa and ma'lul; it only works when the 'illa is a ruling, not a pure description.

This lesson introduces the first type of qalb (inversion) used in Hanafi legal argumentation. Understanding this tool allows you to turn an adversary's proof against them by reversing the causal relationship they established. We will explore the riba example and the case of the Haram refugee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's ta'lil
Determine what the opponent has set as the 'illa (cause) and what as the ma'lul (ruling).
In the riba example, the Shafi'i 'illa is 'occurrence of riba in large quantity' and the ma'lul is 'occurrence in small quantity'.
2
Check if the 'illa is a ruling (hukm)
Type 1 qalb is only valid when the 'illa is a ruling (e.g., prohibition of riba in large) and not a pure description (e.g., red).
A pure description cannot become a ruling.
3
Perform the inversion
Swap the 'illa and ma'lul: make the original 'illa the new ma'lul, and the original ma'lul the new 'illa.
The Hanafi response makes riba in small the 'illa for riba in large.
4
Derive the consequence
Show that the new relationship leads to a contradiction or an absurdity that undermines the opponent's claim.
This reveals that the opponent's analogy is flawed.
5
Conclude the invalidation
The opponent's ta'lil is thereby nullified, and the Hanafi position stands.
The practical effect: Hanafis permit selling a handful for two handfuls in certain cases.

الكثير كالأثمان وكذلك في مسألة الملتجىء بالحرم حرمة إتلاف النفس 
والثوب، وكلاهما يرجعان إلى شيء واحد وهو تغيير هيأة الشيء على خلاف الهيأة التي كان عليها، فكذا في القياس يستعمل القلب الصحيح بمعنيين وكلاهما يرجعان إلى معنى واحد وهو تغيير الدليل إلى هيأة تخالف التي كان عليها، كذا قيل. 
(۱) قوله: [معلولاً لذلك الحكم... إلخ] يعني: ما جعله المعلّل علة جعله السائل معلولاً أي: حكماً ومــــا جعله المعلل معلولاً جعله السائل علة، وفيه إبطال التعليل بإبطال علّته بجعلها حكماً، وإنما يصح هذا النوع من القلب فيما إذا علّل المستدلّ بالحكم بأن جعل ما كان حكماً في الأصل علة لحكم آخر، فأمّا لو علّل بالوصف المحض لا يرد عليه هذا القلب؛ لأنّ الوصف لا يصير حكماً بوجه ولا يصير الحكـــــم الثابت علّةً له؛ لأنه سابق على الحكم، كذا في "المعدن". 
(۲) قوله: [بالحفنتين منه] إلا من جعل الربا في الكثير حراماً في بيع ما يدخل تحت الكيل يوجب جريان الربا القليل كالأثمان، فإنّه يجري فيه الربا في القليل والكثير والجامع أن كلا منهما يجري فيه الربا. 
(۳) قوله: [بل جريان الربا... إلخ] أي: فقد قلبنا تعليل الخصم وجعلنا جريانه في الكثير حكماً وهو علّة في قياس الخصم وجعلنا جريانه في القليل علّة وهو حكم في قياسه، وفيه أنّ القلب إنما يكون في الأصل، والمصنف رحمه قلب في الفرع ويجاب : بأنّ القلب في الفرع يستلزم القلب في الأصل، كذا في "المعدن". 
(٤) قوله: [الملتجيء بالحرم وهو من عليه القصاص في النفس، فإنّه إذا التجى إلى الحرم لا يقتل فيه عندنا لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَن دَخَلَهُ كَانَ آمِناً الآية [آل عمران : ۹۷] إلا أنه لا يطعم ولا يسقى ولا يجالس ولا يباع حتى يضطر إلى الخروج فيقتل خارج الحرم، وعند الشافعي رحمه الله يقتل في الحرم بالقيـــاس على من عليه القصاص في الطرف؛ لأنه إذا التجى إلى الحرم يستوفى منه القصاص اتفاقاً فكذا القصاص في النفس والجامع أنّ كلا منهما جان، قال أصحاب الشافعي رحمه: حرمة إتلاف النفس يوجب حرمة إتلاف الطرف يعني: أنّ حرمة إتلاف النفس علّة لحرمة إتلاف الطرف كصيد الحــــرم؛ حرمة نفسه يوجب حرمة طرفه وحرمة الطرف غير ثابت في الملتجي بالإجماع، فعلم أنّ حرمة 
أي كصيد الحرم.
